PREFACE
         This town code of the Town of Leyden, as supplemented, contains
ordinances up to and including ordinance SWO-2024-9, passed October 8, 2024.
Ordinances of the Town adopted after said ordinance supersede the provisions of
this code to the extent that they are in conflict or inconsistent therewith.
Consult the Town office in order to ascertain whether any particular provision
of the code has been amended, superseded or repealed.
                     American Legal Publishing
                     Cincinnati, Ohio
ORDINANCES PENDING REVIEW FOR CODIFICATION
Listed ordinances have been passed, but they are pending review by the
publisher, and they may not affect the code of ordinances. Additionally,
ordinances listed in this section may not show the original ordinances in their
entirety. Please contact the office of the clerk if there are any questions
concerning any listed ordinances.
 
ORDINANCE NO. SWO 2024-10
 
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLE 5 “WATER AND SEWER SYSTEM”, CHAPTER 4 “RATES AND
CHARGES”, SECTION 3 “COMBINED SYSTEM SERVICE CHARGES ESTABLISHED”, SUBSECTION A
“RATE CLASSIFICATIONS”,
OF THE LEYDEN TOWN CODE
______________________________________________________________________________
   NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE TOWN SUPERVISOR AND THE BOARD OF
TRUSTEES OF THE TOWN OF LEYDEN, COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:
   SECTION 1 :   The corporate authorities of the Town of Leyden (the “Town”)
adopt and approve an amendment to Title 5 “Water and Sewer System”, Chapter 4
“Rates and Charges”, Section 3 “Combined System Service Charges Established”,
Subsection A “Rate Classifications” of the Town Code to state as follows:
5-4-3: COMBINED SYSTEM SERVICE CHARGES ESTABLISHED:
   A.   Rate Classifications:
      1.   Each residential dwelling unit within an individual building
containing not more than three (3) separate dwelling units shall be charged at
the residential rate for water and sewer use.
2. All buildings and properties owned by a nonprofit tax-exempt organization or
a for-profit entity that are exclusively used for multifamily senior housing,
that qualified for the Illinois Affordable Housing Tax Credit (20 ILCS 3805/
7.28, as may be amended), and that contain more than three (3) separate
dwelling units, including each residential dwelling unit within said buildings
and properties, shall be charged at the residential rate for water and sewer
use.
      3.   All buildings and properties owned and occupied by a taxing district
for governmental, Municipal, library or school use shall be charged at the
Municipal rate for water and sewer use.
      4.   All buildings and properties occupied by a charitable, religious or
not for profit organization that is an exempt organization under section 501(c)
of the Internal Revenue Code, and actually and exclusively used for charitable,
religious or beneficent purposes, shall be charged at the Municipal rate for
water and sewer use.
      5.   All buildings, properties and customers which are not classified
within the residential or Municipal rate classifications, shall be classified
as commercial customers and charged at the commercial rate for water and sewer
use.  
6. Each residential dwelling unit, Municipal rate customer premises and
commercial rate customer premises that is verified to be vacant and unoccupied
for more than ninety (90) days, or is currently suspended from water service or
sewer service, shall be charged the reactivation fee as noted in F, 3 of this
section. 
*   *   *
 
   SECTION 2:   This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after
its passage as provided by law.
   PASSED this 12th day of November, 2024.
   AYES:      
   NAYS:
   ABSENT:         
            
                     ______________________________
                           Supervisor
 
 
ATTEST:
 
______________________________
   Town Clerk
         
 
      
 
 
 
ORDINANCE NO. TO 2024-16
 
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLE 1 “ADMINISTRATIVE”, CHAPTER 6 “TOWNSHIP OFFICERS
AND EMPLOYEES”, SECTION 6 “SALARIES OF OFFICERS” OF THE LEYDEN TOWN CODE
_____________________________________________________________________________                                                                                                                                                         
   
   NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE SUPERVISOR AND BOARD OF TRUSTEES OF
THE TOWN OF LEYDEN, COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:
   SECTION 1: The corporate authorities of the Town of Leyden (the “Town”)
adopt and approve an amendment to Title 1 “Administrative”, Chapter 6 “Township
Officers and Employees”, Section 6 “Salaries of Officers” of the Leyden Town
Code to state as follows:
1-6-6:   SALARIES OF OFFICERS:
 
A.   Township Supervisor: The salary and compensation of the supervisor, whose
term of office will commence on or after the third Monday of May 2025, is
established as follows:
 
1.   An annual salary of forty-four thousand dollars ($44,000.00) for services
as supervisor, treasurer of the township road district, ex officio treasurer of
combined waterworks and sewerage system, and as the ex-officio supervisor of
general assistance, payable from the following funds:
 
a.    General town fund: twenty thousand dollars ($20,000.00).
 
b.    Road and bridge fund: one thousand dollars ($1,000.00).
 
c.    Sewer and water fund: twenty thousand dollars ($20,000.00).
 
d.    General assistance fund: three thousand dollars ($3,000.00).
 
B.   Township Trustees:   The salary and compensation of each township trustee,
whose term of office will commence on or after the third Monday of May 2025, is
established as follows:
 
   1.   An annual salary of twelve thousand dollars ($12,000.00) for services
as township trustee.
      
   
 
 
C. Township Clerk: The salary and compensation of the Township Clerk, whose
term of office will commence on or after the third Monday of May 2025, is
established as follows:
 
1.    An annual salary of seventy-eight thousand dollars ($78,000.00) for
services as the town clerk.
 
   2.   Health, hospitalization, and accident insurance benefits based upon
established township policy.
 
   3.   Membership in the Illinois Municipal Retirement Fund and the benefits
pertaining thereto as provided by law.
 
D.   Township Highway Commissioner: The salary and compensation of the highway
commissioner, whose term of office will commence on or after the third Monday
of May 2025, is established as follows:
 
   1.   An annual salary of twenty thousand dollars ($20,000.00) for services
as the township highway commissioner.
 
E.   Township Assessor: The annual salary and compensation of the township
assessor, whose term of office will commence on January 1, 2026, is established
as follows:
 
   1.   An annual salary of thirty-one thousand dollars ($31,000.00) for
services as the township assessor.
   
   2.   Health, hospitalization, and accident insurance benefits based upon
established township policy.
 
   3.   Membership in the Illinois Municipal Retirement Fund and the benefits
pertaining thereto as provided by law.
 
F.    Expense Reimbursement: The persons duly elected or appointed to the
offices provided herein shall be reimbursed for all properly audited out of
pocket expenses necessarily incurred in the conduct of the official business
for the town and in the fulfillment of the duties of such person’s office.
 
 
 
SECTION 2: This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after its
passage as provided by law; provided, however, that this Ordinance shall be
effective for the terms of office that will commence on or after the third
Monday of May 2025.
   
PASSED this 12 th day of November 2024.

ORDINANCE NO. SWO 2025-3
 
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLE 5 “WATER AND SEWER SYSTEM”, CHAPTER 4 “RATES AND
CHARGES”, SECTION 3 “COMBINED SYSTEM SERVICE CHARGES ESTABLISHED” OF THE LEYDEN
TOWN CODE TO INCREASE COMBINED SEWER AND WATER RATES
______________________________________________________________________________
   WHEREAS, the Town of Leyden (the “Town”) operates a combined water and sewer
system (the “System”); and
   WHEREAS, the Town’s water supply is provided by the City of Chicago; and
   WHEREAS, the City of Chicago recently increased its water rates; and
   WHEREAS, due to the City of Chicago’s increased water rates, the Town’s
corporate authorities find that it is in the Town’s best interests to increase
the System’s water rates as provided by this ordinance; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE TOWN SUPERVISOR AND THE BOARD OF TRUSTEES
OF THE TOWN OF LEYDEN, COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:
   SECTION 1 :   The Town’s corporate authorities adopt and approve an
amendment to Title 5 “Water and Sewer System”, Chapter 4 “Rates and Charges”,
Section 3 “Combined System Service Charges Established” of the Town Code to
state in its entirety as follows:
5-4-3: COMBINED SYSTEM SERVICE CHARGES ESTABLISHED:
 A.   Rate Classifications:
      1.   Each residential dwelling unit within an individual building
containing not more than three (3) separate dwelling units shall be charged at
the residential rate for water and sewer use.
      2.   All buildings and properties owned by a nonprofit tax-exempt
organization that are exclusively used for multifamily senior housing,
qualified for the Illinois Affordable Housing Tax Credit (20 ILCS 3805/7.28, as
may be amended), and contain more than three (3) separate dwelling units,
including each residential dwelling until within said buildings and properties,
shall be charged at the residential rate for water and sewer use.
      3.   All buildings and properties owned and occupied by a taxing district
for governmental, Municipal, library or school use shall be charged at the
Municipal rate for water and sewer use.
      4.   All buildings and properties occupied by a charitable, religious or
not for profit organization that is an exempt organization under section 501(c)
of the Internal Revenue Code, and actually and exclusively used for charitable,
religious or beneficent purposes, shall be charged at the Municipal rate for
water and sewer use.
      5.   All buildings, properties and customers which are not classified
within the residential or Municipal rate classifications, shall be classified
as commercial customers and charged at the commercial rate for water and sewer
use.
      6.   Each residential dwelling unit, Municipal rate customer premises and
commercial rate customer premises that is verified to be vacant and unoccupied
for more than ninety (90) days, or is currently suspended from water service or
sewer service, shall be charged the reactivation fee as noted in F.3. of this
section.
   B.   Residential Rate: Effective with the billing cycle commencing July 1,
2025:
      1.   The minimum combined water use and sewer service charge for all
residential rate customers is hereby fixed and established as forty dollars and
fifty-nine cents ($40.59) per monthly billing period, based upon actual or
estimated meter readings of water furnished to the user for the monthly billing
period up to, but not exceeding, three thousand (3,000) gallons.
      2.   The water and sewer user charge for usage in excess of three
thousand (3,000) gallons of water furnished a month shall be at the following
rates:
         a.   Water user charge: Eleven dollars and ninety-two cents ($11.92)
per one thousand (1,000) gallons.
         b.   Sewer user charge: One dollar and sixty-one cents ($1.61) per one
thousand (1,000) gallons.
   C.   Municipal Rate: Effective with the billing cycle commencing July 1,
2025:
      1.   The minimum combined water use and sewer service charge for all
Municipal rate customers is hereby fixed and established as forty-six dollars
and sixty-two cents ($46.62) per monthly billing period, based upon actual or
estimated meter readings of water furnished to the user for the monthly billing
period up to, but not exceeding, three thousand (3,000) gallons.
      2.   The water and sewer user charge for usage in excess of three
thousand (3,000) gallons of water furnished a month shall be at the following
rates:
         a.   Water user charge: Thirteen dollars and forty-three cents
($13.43) per one thousand (1,000) gallons.
         b.   Sewer user charge: Two dollars and eleven cents ($2.11) per one
thousand (1,000) gallons.
   D.   Commercial Rate: Effective with the billing cycle commencing July 1,
2025:
      1.   The minimum combined water use and sewer service charge for all
commercial rate customers is hereby fixed and established as one hundred twenty
dollars and eighteen cents ($120.18) per monthly billing period, based upon
actual or estimated meter readings of water furnished to the user for the
monthly billing period up to, but not exceeding, three thousand (3,000)
gallons.
      2.   The water and sewer user charge for usage in excess of three
thousand (3,000) gallons of water furnished a month shall be at the following
rates:
         a.   Water user charge: Eighteen dollars and sixty-two cents ($18.62)
per one thousand (1,000) gallons.
         b.   Sewer user charge: Two dollars and eleven cents ($2.11) per one
thousand (1,000) gallons.
   E.   Suspended Rate: Effective with the billing cycle commencing July 15,
2020:
      1.   The water user charge for all residential and Municipal suspended
rate customers is hereby fixed and established as twenty dollars ($20.00) per
monthly billing period.
      2.   The water user charge for all commercial suspended rate customers is
hereby fixed and established as forty dollars ($40.00) per monthly billing
period.
      3.   The sewer user charge for residential and Municipal suspended rate
customers shall be five dollars ($5.00) per month.
      4.   The sewer user charge for all commercial suspended rate customers
shall be ten dollars ($10.00) per month.
   F.   Service Charges: The following charges shall be effective with the
billing cycle commencing July 15, 2020, and shall be applied to all customers:
      1.   One hundred dollars ($100.00) for missed appointments to turn on
water service. An appointment will not be considered missed if the customer
calls the main number of the Township (847-455-8616) during business hours not
later than one (1) full business day prior to the turn on appointment to cancel
or reschedule the appointment.
      2.   One hundred dollars ($100.00) for missed appointments for meter
inspection. An appointment will not be considered missed if the customer calls
the main number of the Township (847-455-8616) during business hours not later
than one (1) full business day prior to the meter inspection to cancel or
reschedule the appointment.
      3.   The reactivation of service to the premises of a suspended rate
account shall be subject to payment of the account balance associated with the
premises, and a reconnection fee as follows:
         a.   Seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for accounts with a balance
due of less than five thousand dollars ($5,000.00).
         b.   One thousand dollars ($1,000.00) for accounts with a balance due
between five thousand dollars ($5,000.00) and ten thousand dollars
($10,000.00).
         c.   One thousand five hundred dollars ($1,500.00) for accounts with a
balance due of more than ten thousand dollars ($10,000.00).
      4.   The fee for replacing a missing or damaged water meter is six
hundred fifty dollars ($650.00).
      5.   The fee for replacing a missing or damaged MTU is four hundred fifty
dollars ($450.00).
      6.   The fee for unauthorized removal or tampering with a meter or MTU
shall not be less than twenty-five dollars ($25.00) and no more than one
thousand dollars ($1,000.00), plus the applicable replacement fee.
      7.   Water service to a residential dwelling unit, Municipal rate
customer premises or commercial rate customer premises may be terminated for a
period of time upon written request and payment of a five hundred dollar
($500.00) winterization fee.
   G.   Sanitary Sewer Service Only Rate: Effective with the billing cycle
commencing July 1, 2025, the minimum sewer service charge is hereby fixed and
established as four hundred five dollars and forty-six cents ($405.46) per
monthly billing period for all Municipal and commercial rate customers who only
receive sanitary sewer service.
   H.   Senior Freeze Minimum Monthly Rate: Effective with the billing cycle
commencing July 1, 2025:
      1.   The minimum combined water use and sewer service charge for all
residential rate customers receiving a senior freeze exemption on their second
installment residential Real Estate Tax bill is hereby fixed and established as
thirty dollars and eighty-one cents ($30.81) per monthly billing period, based
upon actual or estimated meter reading of water furnished to the user for the
monthly billing period up to, but not exceeding, three thousand (3,000)
gallons.
      2.   Application for the senior freeze minimum monthly rate is required
annually for the rate applied each January 1 through December 31. The senior
freeze minimum monthly rate application period for each year starts on each
December 15 of the prior year and closes on January 31 of the next year (e.g.,
December 15, 2022, through January 31, 2023).
      3.   Transfer of owner interest at any time will immediately move the
monthly minimum rate to the rate established in subsection B.1. of this
section.
   I.   Connection Fees: The charge for each initial connection to the combined
system shall be based upon the diameter of the pipe furnishing water service,
as follows:
 
 
 1 inch diameter   $1,500.00
1 1/2 inch diameter $2,500.00
2 inch diameter     $4,000.00
3 inch diameter     $5,000.00
4 inch diameter     $7,500.00
6 inch diameter     $10,500.00
8 inch diameter     $14,000.00
    J.   Additional Connection And Disconnection Fees:
      1.   Additional Connection Fees: The charge for each connection after the
initial connection to the combined system shall be the cost incurred by the
Superintendent in making such connection.
      2.   Disconnection Fees: The cost of building sewer and water service
line disconnections from the combined system performed by the Township shall be
as follows:
 
 
 Residential building sewer and/or water service $2,500.00
line
Commercial building sewers and/or water service   $5,000.00, or time and
lines                                             material cost plus $500.00,
                                                  whichever is greater
                                                  $5,000.00, or time and
Fire suppression systems                          material cost plus $500.00,
                                                  whichever is greater
When contracted by Township                       Contractor fee plus 10%
    K.   Estimated Charges; Interest On Unpaid Bills:
      1.   In cases where it shall be found that a water or sewer meter has
registered incorrectly or has stopped because of malfunctioning equipment, the
charges and payments for sewer and water services shall be made on an estimate
prepared by the Superintendent based upon the average of four (4) preceding
readings of such meter, excluding excessive or obviously substantial deficient
readings. Where such meter has been installed for less than one (1) year or
where less than four (4) competent readings exist, such estimate may be based
upon a lesser number of the four (4) preceding readings of such meter prior to
such incorrect or stopped registration. Where such readings shall be found
excessive or substantially deficient, the Superintendent is authorized to
establish a billing which shall be due and payable when billed. The
Superintendent may also include a reasonable charge for interest on unpaid
sewer and water charges at a rate not to exceed 1.5% per month.
      2.   Estimated Charges; Interest On Unpaid Bills: In cases where it shall
be found that a water or sewer meter has been tampered with or where any
instrument, device or apparatus has been installed that causes diversion,
interference, or inaccurate measurement of utility services, the charges and
payments for sewer and water services shall be made on an estimate prepared by
the Superintendent based upon the average of four (4) preceding readings of
such meter, excluding excessive or obviously substantial deficient readings.
Where such meter has been installed for less than one (1) year where less than
four (4) competent readings exist, such estimate may be based upon a lesser
number of the four (4) preceding readings of such meter prior to such
tampering. Where such readings shall be found excessive or substantially
deficient, the Superintendent is authorized to establish a billing which shall
be due and payable when billed. The Superintendent may also include a
reasonable charge for interest on unpaid sewer and water charges at a rate not
to exceed 5% per month.
   L.   Adjustments: No Town employee is authorized to adjust bills for sewer
and water service from that required by application of the appropriate charges
to actual meter readings, except as may be authorized in writing by the
Superintendent. The Superintendent may, in writing, authorize adjustments to a
user's bill, if the Superintendent determines that the actual meter readings
are excessive, the appropriate charges were not correctly applied to actual
meter readings, or the adjustments are otherwise appropriate in the
Superintendent's judgment.
   M.   Water Surcharge; Exclusive Service Violations: In cases where it shall
be found that a user of the combined system is taking water service from
another utility system or source in violation of subsection 5-1-5 A. of this
title, a surcharge shall be imposed and charged to the user on all estimated
quantities of water that such user receives or previously received from such
other utility or source at the water user charge rate set forth in subsection
B.1. of this section.
   N.   Changes In Status Of Not For Profit Customers:
      1.   All not for profit organizations that desire to be charged for sewer
and water service at the municipal rate provided in this section shall submit a
written application and any supporting material required by the township to
establish to the satisfaction of the township that: a) the buildings or
properties occupied by the applicant are actually and exclusively used for
charitable, religious or beneficent purposes, and b) that the applicant is a
qualified organization under section 501(c) of the internal revenue code.
      2.   All buildings, properties and customers that are classified as not
for profit organizations and uses and that are charged at the municipal rate
shall be reclassified as commercial customers and charged at the commercial
rate for water and sewer use at such time as:
         a.   The customer loses its 501(c) status;
         b.   The building or property is no longer used exclusively for
charitable, religious or beneficent purposes; or
         c.   The organization is unable to establish to the satisfaction of
the township that it is entitled to be charged at the municipal rate for water
and sewer use as provided under subsection A3 of this section.
      3.   Any organization that has applied and received the municipal rate
for water and sewer use as a not for profit organization under this section
shall notify the township supervisor in writing within five (5) business days
of any change in its status under section 501(c) of the internal revenue code,
of any change in its use or occupancy of a building or property that is
receiving water charged at the municipal rate, or of any other circumstance or
event that disqualifies the organization from receiving sewer and water service
from the township at the municipal rate provided in subsection A3 of this
section.
      4.   Failure of a water customer to give written notice to the township
as required under subsection N3 of this section is a violation of this section
which shall result in an enforcement surcharge of two hundred fifty dollars
($250.00) being added to the customer's current account, in addition to any
other fees or charges that may be due from the customer. An adjusted water bill
shall be issued to the customer charging the customer the difference between
the commercial rate and the municipal rate for customer's water and sewer use
for the period of time that the customer was not eligible to be charged at the
municipal rate for water and sewer use, together with interest at the rate of
1.5% for each month, or part of a month, that the customer was disqualified
from receiving sewer and water service at the municipal rate.
 
   SECTION 2:   This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after
its passage as provided by law.
   PASSED this 10th day of June, 2025.
   AYES:      
   NAYS:
   ABSENT:

ORDINANCE NO. TO 2025-3
 
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLE 3 “PUBLIC HEALTH SAFETY AND PROTECTION”, CHAPTER 2
“PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE”, TO ADD SECTION 19 “SEASONAL DECORATIONS” OF THE
LEYDEN TOWN CODE
_____________________________________________________________________________                                                                                                                                                         
   
   NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE SUPERVISOR AND BOARD OF TRUSTEES OF
THE TOWN OF LEYDEN, COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:
   SECTION 1: The corporate authorities of the Town of Leyden (the “Town”)
adopt and approve an amendment to Title 3 “Public Health Safety and
Protection”, Chapter 2 “Property Maintenance Code”, Section 19 “Seasonal
Decorations” of the Leyden Town Code to state as follows:
3-2-19:    SEASONAL DECORATIONS:
 
No person shall display exterior items of a primarily decorative nature visible
from the public right-of-way and associated with the celebration of seasonal
events or holidays earlier than 90 calendar days before, and 90 calendars
after, the seasonal event or holiday.
 
Any person found to have been in violation of this section shall be fined not
less than $50.00 nor more than $500.00 for each offense.
 
   SECTION 2:   This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect immediately
upon its passage and approval as provided by law.
PASSED this 8 th day of April 2025.
   AYES:
   NAYS:
   ABSENT:                
 
 
_________ _________________________
                        Supervisor
ATTEST:
 
________ _________________________
      Township Clerk
 
 
 
ORDINANCE NO. TO 2025-5
 
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLE 3 “PUBLIC HEALTH, SAFETY AND PROTECTION”, CHAPTER 4
“WASTE DISPOSAL REGULATIONS”, SECTION 11 “BILLS FOR SERVICES; DELINQUENCIES” OF
THE LEYDEN TOWN CODE TO INCREASE WASTE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL RATES
______________________________________________________________________________
WHEREAS, the Town of Leyden (the “Town”) charges for waste collection and
disposal services provided to covered customers by the Town’s licensed waste
hauler; and
   WHEREAS, the Town’s licensed waste hauler recently increased its rates for
waste collection and disposal services; and
   WHEREAS, the Town’s corporate authorities find that it is in the Town’s best
interests to increase the waste collection and disposal services rates as
provided by this ordinance; and
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE TOWN SUPERVISOR AND THE BOARD OF TRUSTEES
OF THE TOWN OF LEYDEN, COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:
   SECTION 1 :   The Town’s corporate authorities adopt and approve an
amendment to Title 3 “Public Health, Safety and Protection”, Chapter 4 “Waste
Disposal Regulations”, Section 11 “Bills for Services; Delinquencies” of the
Town Code to state in its entirety as follows:
3-4-11: BILLS FOR SERVICE; DELINQUENCIES:
   A.   Payment Of Charges: Charges for waste collection and disposal services
provided to covered units/customers by the Town's licensed waste hauler,
penalty charges as provided in section 3-4-12 of this chapter, and charges for
the abatement of any nuisance by the Town, as provided in section 3-4-10 of
this chapter, shall be included and billed as part of the Town's periodic bill
for sewer and water utility service to the subject property, and shall be paid
at the Town hall within fifteen (15) days after the billing date. The owner of
the subject property, and any nonowner who is the occupant or the lessee
thereof, shall be jointly and severally liable to pay for waste collection and
disposal services provided to the premises and any charges for the abatement of
a nuisance as provided herein.
 
      1.   Covered units/customers shall be charged the fees set forth in the
agreement between the Town and a waste hauler for waste collection and disposal
services; provided, however, that the charges for non-senior residential units
shall be twenty-three dollars and twenty-one cents ($23.21) and senior
residential units shall be twenty-one dollars and sixty-five cents ($21.65) for
the billing cycle commencing on July 1, 2025.
 
   B.   Late Charge: For late charges, see subsection 5-4-4 E of this code.
 
   C.   Disconnection Of Utility Service For Failure To Pay Bill: If the owner,
occupant or lessee has not paid the charges for unpaid waste collection and
disposal services, penalty charges or the charges for abatement of a nuisance,
within thirty (30) days of the date of the issuance of the bill for such costs,
utility service to the subject property may be disconnected by the town
supervisor in accordance with the procedures set forth in section 5-1-11 of
this code.
 
   D.   Charges A Debt; Lien For Charges: The charges for unpaid waste
collection and disposal, penalty charges and any charges for abatement of a
nuisance billed in accordance with this section by the town to the owner,
occupant or lessee of the subject property shall be a debt due to the town. If
the charges are not paid within thirty (30) days after they are due, they shall
be deemed delinquent and shall be a lien upon the real estate as provided in
section 5-4-4 of this code. A change of ownership or occupancy of premises
found delinquent shall not be cause for reducing or eliminating these charges
or any penalties.
 
   SECTION 2:   This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after
its passage as provided by law.
   PASSED this 10th day of June, 2025.
   AYES:      
   NAYS:
   ABSENT:         
                     ______________________________
                           Supervisor
ATTEST:

   Town Clerk
 
 
 
 
ORDINANCE NO. TO 2025-6
 
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING TITLE 2 “BUSINESS AND LICENSE REGULATIONS”, CHAPTER 1
“JUNK DEALERS AND PEDDLERS” OF THE LEYDEN TOWN CODE TO MAKE VARIOUS CHANGES
______________________________________________________________________________
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED BY THE TOWN SUPERVISOR AND THE BOARD OF TRUSTEES
OF THE TOWN OF LEYDEN, COOK COUNTY, ILLINOIS, as follows:
   SECTION 1 :   The Town of Leyden’s corporate authorities adopt and approve
an amendment to Title 2 “Business and License Regulations”, Chapter 2 “Junk
Dealers and Peddlers” of the Town Code to state in its entirety as follows:
2-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this Chapter, the following word or words shall have the meanings
ascribed to them in this Section:
JUNK: Old iron, chain, brass, copper, tin, lead or other base metals; old rope,
bags, rags, wastepaper, paper clippings, scraps of woolens, clips, bagging,
rubber and glass, and empty bottles; and all articles and things discarded or
no longer used as manufactured articles composed of any one or more of the
articles herein mentioned.
JUNK DEALERS: Every person engaged in the business of wholesale junk dealer,
retail junk dealer or junk peddler.
JUNK PEDDLER: Any person who uses a junk wagon for the purpose of buying,
selling or bartering in junk.
JUNK STORE: Any premises, shop, warehouse or building occupied for the conduct
of the business of wholesale or retail junk dealer.
JUNK WAGON: Every junk wagon, truck, automobile, pushcart or other vehicle used
in the conduct of the business of a junk dealer.
JUNK YARD: Any yard, place or enclosure, other than a junk store, occupied for
the conduct of the business of wholesale or retail junk dealer.
RETAIL JUNK DEALER: Every person engaged in buying, selling or bartering junk
in quantities of less than the amounts dealt in by wholesale junk dealers at
premises leased or purchased especially for the purpose of conducting such
business.
WHOLESALE JUNK DEALER: Every person engaged in the business of buying, selling
or bartering junk in quantities of ten (10) tons or more of metal junk; or ten
(10) bales or more of rags or paper; or correspondingly large lots of any other
junk at premises leased or purchased especially for the purpose of conducting
such business.
2-1-2: LICENSES REQUIRED:
A person who has obtained and possesses a valid license from the County of Cook
to be engaged in the business of a junk dealer shall be deemed to have
satisfied the licensing requirement of this Chapter. No other person shall be
engaged in the business of a junk dealer without first obtaining a license from
the Supervisor.
2-1-3: APPLICATION FOR LICENSE:
Application for a license under this Chapter shall be made in conformity with
general requirements specified by the Town Supervisor, and shall include but
shall not be limited to the following items:
A. Type of business.
B. Location of business.
C. Statement by applicant that the applicant has not been convicted of
receiving stolen property in violation of the laws of the State of Illinois; or
if applicant is a corporation, a statement by an officer of the corporation
that none of applicant’s officers, stockholders or employees has been convicted
of receiving stolen property in violation of the laws of the State of Illinois.
The Supervisor shall direct the issuance of licenses only to such persons as
shall produce satisfactory evidence of good character and responsible standing.
2-1-4: LICENSE FEES:
A. Retail Junk Dealers: The annual fee for a retail junk dealer's license shall
be as follows:
 
3,200 sq. ft. or less                            $100.00
                                                  
Over 3,200 sq. ft. but less than 6,400 sq. ft.   $150.00
Over 6,400 sq. ft. but less than 9,600 sq. ft.   $200.00
Over 9,600 sq. ft. but less than 12,800 sq. ft.  $300.00
Over 12,000 sq. ft. but less than 16,000 sq. ft. $400.00
Over 16,000 sq. ft.                              $500.00
   
Where the business is conducted upon more than one floor, the total square foot
area shall be based upon the area of each floor.
B. Wholesale Junk Dealers: The annual fee for a wholesale junk dealer's license
shall be five hundred dollars ($500.00).
C. Junk Vehicles: A separate license shall be obtained for each junk wagon at
an annual fee of one hundred dollars ($100.00) each.
2-1-5: CONDITIONS OF LICENSE:
A. License to be Displayed: The Town Clerk shall issue an appropriate insignia
designating the type of license issued to applicant which shall be prominently
displayed on the premises of the junk store or junk yard, or upon the junk
wagon of any such junk dealer or junk peddler.
B. Hours of Operation: No junk dealer shall receive junk from any person
between the hours of seven o’clock (7:00) P.M. and seven o’clock(7:00) A.M.,
nor shall he sell, purchase or collect any junk in any public alley between the
hours of five o’clock (5:00) P.M. and seven o’clock (7:00) A.M.
C. Purchase from Other Junk Dealers: No person licensed as a retail junk dealer
shall be permitted under a retail junk dealer’s license to purchase junk from
another retail junk dealer.
D. Receipt of Junk, Holding Period:
1. Every wholesale junk dealer who is also a retail junk dealer shall keep all
junk purchased in retail quantities separate and distinct from wholesale junk
for a period of two (2) days during which time said retail junk shall be open
to inspection of any member of the Township’s law enforcing authorities, and no
such junk shall be melted, vulcanized or otherwise changed in form or its
identity destroyed within such time.
2. No junk dealer shall sell or dispose of any junk within two (2) days of the
time of collecting, receiving or purchasing same, excepting, however, sales of
a junk peddler to a retail junk dealer whose duty it shall be to hold such
purchases for the two (2) days as herein provided.
E. Purchase from Minors: No junk dealer shall purchase any articles whatsoever
from any minor without the written consent of the minor’s parent or guardian.
The penalty for such violation shall be a fine of not less than one dollar
($1.00) nor more than fifty dollars ($50.00) for each offense.
2-1-6: LOCATION AND PREMISES REGULATIONS:
A. Location Restrictions: It shall be unlawful for any person:
1. To locate any junk store or junk yard within four hundred feet (400') of a
church, hospital, public or parochial school measured by the shortest straight
line between the junk store or junk yard and any such building.
2. To locate any junk store or junk yard in any block in which two-thirds (2/3)
of the buildings on both sides of the street on such block are used exclusively
for residence purposes or for wholesale or retail store purposes, without the
written consents of a majority of the property owners according to frontage on
both sides of the street, including buildings located upon the corner lots of
said street regardless of where they front; provided however, that the word
"block" means only that part of the street in question which lies between the
two (2) nearest intersecting streets on either side of the street on which said
junk store or junk yard is to be located.
3. To locate, conduct or operate any junk store or junk yard upon any street in
the Town upon which is located a bus line.
B. Junk Yards to be Fenced: Every junk yard shall be surrounded by a solid
fence, eight feet (8') high, which is so constructed as to completely obscure
the area enclosed and the materials stored therein. Such fence shall be located
at least eight feet (8') from all public ways surrounding the property and none
of said materials shall be piled nearer than six inches (6") to nor higher than
such fence.
2-1-7: JUNK VEHICLES:
Each junk wagon shall be prominently marked with the name of the junk dealer
using such junk wagon together with the street and number of the junk dealer’s
place of business.
2-1-8: INSPECTIONS:
The place of business and the junk wagons of all junk dealers shall at all
reasonable times be open to the inspection of any member of the Township law
enforcing authorities.
2-1-9: REVOCATION OF LICENSE:
The license of any person licensed as a junk dealer who is convicted of
receiving stolen goods or property shall, upon conviction, be immediately
revoked.
2-1-10: PENALTIES:
Any person who violates any of the provisions of this Chapter shall be fined
not less than twenty-five dollars ($25.00) nor more than five hundred dollars
($500.00) for each offense, and every day on which such violation continues
shall constitute a separate and distinct offense.
 
   SECTION 2:   This Ordinance shall be in full force and effect from and after
its passage as provided by law.
   PASSED this 10th day of June, 2025.
   AYES:      
   NAYS:
   ABSENT:         
                     ______________________________
                           Supervisor
ATTEST:
 
______________________________
   Town Clerk
 
 
TITLE 1
ADMINISTRATIVE
CHAPTER 1
OFFICIAL TOWNSHIP CODE
SECTION:
1-1-1: Title
1-1-2: Acceptance
1-1-3: Amendments
1-1-4: Code Alterations
1-1-1: TITLE:
   Upon adoption by the Town Board of Trustees, this Code is hereby declared to
be and shall hereinafter constitute the official Code of the Town of Leyden.
This Code of ordinances shall be known and cited as the LEYDEN TOWN CODE, and
it is hereby published by authority of the Town Board and shall be kept up to
date as provided in Section 1-1-3 of this Chapter. Any reference to the number
of any section contained herein shall be understood to refer to the position of
the same number, its appropriate chapter and title heading, and to the general
penalty clause, relating thereto, as well as to the section itself, when
reference is made to this Town Code by title in any legal documents. (1992
Code)
1-1-2: ACCEPTANCE:
   The Town Code, as hereby presented in printed form, shall hereafter be
received without further proof in all courts and in all administrative
tribunals of this State as the ordinances of the Township of general and
permanent effect, except the excluded ordinances enumerated in Section
1-2-1 of this Code. (1992 Code)
1-1-3: AMENDMENTS:
   Any ordinance amending the Town Code shall set forth the title, chapter and
section number of the section or sections to be amended, and this shall
constitute sufficient compliance with any statutory requirement pertaining to
the amendment or revision by ordinance of any part of this Town Code. All such
amendments or revisions by ordinance shall be immediately forwarded to the
codifiers and the said ordinance material shall be prepared for insertion in
its proper place in each copy of this Town Code. Each such replacement page
shall be properly identified and shall be inserted in each individual copy of
the Town Code. (1992 Code)
1-1-4: CODE ALTERATIONS:
   It shall be deemed unlawful for any person to alter, change, replace or
deface in any way any section or any page of this Town Code in such a manner
that the meaning of any phrase or order may be changed or omitted. Replacement
pages may be inserted according to the official instructions when so authorized
by the Town Board of Trustees. The Town Clerk shall see that the replacement
pages are properly inserted in the official copies maintained in the office of
the Clerk. Any person having custody of an official copy of the Town Code shall
make every effort to maintain said Code in an up to date and efficient manner,
and shall see to the immediate insertion of new or replacement pages when such
are delivered or made available to said person by the Town Clerk. Said Code
books, while in actual possession of officials and other interested persons,
shall be and remain the property of the Township and shall be returned to the
office of the Clerk when directed so to do by order of the Town Board of
Trustees. (1992 Code; amd. Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022)
CHAPTER 2
SAVING CLAUSE
SECTION:
1-2-1: Repeal of General Ordinances
1-2-2: Court Proceedings
1-2-3: Severability Clause
1-2-1: REPEAL OF GENERAL ORDINANCES:
   All general ordinances of the Township passed prior to the adoption of this
Town Code are hereby repealed, except such as are included in this Town Code or
are by necessary implication herein reserved from repeal (subject to the saving
clauses contained in the following sections), and excluding the following
ordinances which are not hereby repealed: tax levy ordinances; budget and
appropriation ordinances; ordinances dealing with the transfer and expenditure
of funds; contract ordinances and ordinances authorizing the execution of a
contract or the issuance of warrants; salary ordinances; improvement
ordinances; bond ordinances; ordinances relating to elections; ordinances
relating to the transfer or acceptance of real estate by or from the Township;
and all special ordinances. (1992 Code)
1-2-2: COURT PROCEEDINGS:
   No new ordinance shall be construed or held to repeal a former ordinance
whether such former ordinance is expressly repealed or not, as to any offense
committed against such former ordinance or as to any act done, any penalty,
forfeiture or punishment so incurred, or any right accrued or claim arising
under the former ordinance, or in any way whatever to affect any such offense
or act so committed or so done, or any penalty, forfeiture or punishment so
incurred or any right accrued or claim arising before the new ordinance takes
effect, save only that the proceedings thereafter shall conform to the
ordinance in force at the time of such proceeding. So far as practicable, if
any penalty, forfeiture or punishment be mitigated by any provision of a new
ordinance, such provision may be, by consent of the party affected, applied to
any judgment announced after the new ordinance takes effect.
   This Section shall extend to all repeals, either by express words or
implication, whether the repeal is in the ordinance making any new provisions
upon the same subject or in any other ordinance.
   Nothing contained in this Title shall be construed as abating any action now
pending under or by virtue of any general ordinance of the City herein repealed
and the provisions of all general ordinances contained in this Code shall be
deemed to be continuing provisions and not a new enactment of the same
provision; nor shall this Title be deemed as discontinuing, abating, modifying
or altering any penalty accrued or to accrue, or as affecting the liability of
any person, firm or corporation, or as waiving any right of the Township under
any ordinance or provision thereof in force at the time of the adoption of this
Town Code. (1992 Code)
1-2-3: SEVERABILITY CLAUSE:
   If any section, subsection, subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or
phrase of this Town Code or any part thereof is for any reason held to be
unconstitutional or invalid or ineffective by any court of competent
jurisdiction, such decision shall not affect the validity or effectiveness of
the remaining portions of this Code, or any part thereof. The Town Board of
Trustees hereby declares that it would have passed each section, subsection,
subdivision, paragraph, sentence, clause or phrase thereof irrespective of the
fact that any one or more sections, subsections, subdivisions, paragraphs,
sentences, clauses or phrases be declared unconstitutional, invalid or
ineffective. (1992 Code)
CHAPTER 3
DEFINITIONS
SECTION:
1-3-1: Construction of Words
1-3-2: Definitions, General
1-3-3: Intent
1-3-4: Catchlines
1-3-1: CONSTRUCTION OF WORDS:
   Whenever any word in any section of this Town Code importing the plural
number is used in describing or referring to any matters, parties or persons,
any single matter, party or person shall be deemed to be included, although
distributive words may not have been used. When any subject matter, party or
person is referred to in this Town Code by words importing the singular number
only, or the masculine gender, several matters, parties or persons and females
as well as males and bodies corporate shall be deemed to be included; provided,
that these rules of construction shall not be applied to any section of this
Town Code which contains any express provision excluding such construction or
where the subject matter or context may be repugnant thereto.
   The word "ordinance" contained in the ordinances of the Township has been
changed in the content of this Town Code to "Title", "Chapter", "Section" and/
or "subsection" or words of like import for organizational and clarification
purposes only. Such change to the Township's ordinances is not meant to amend
passage and effective dates of such original ordinances. (1992 Code)
1-3-2: DEFINITIONS, GENERAL:
   Whenever the following words or terms are used in this Code, they shall have
such meanings herein ascribed to them, unless the context makes such meaning
repugnant thereto:
   AGENT: A person acting on behalf of another.
   BOARD: Unless otherwise indicated, the Board of Trustees of Leyden Township.
   CODE: The Town Code of Leyden Township.
   COUNTY: Cook County, Illinois.
   EMPLOYEES: Whenever reference is made in this Code to a Township employee by
title only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of Leyden
Township".
   FEE: A sum of money charged by the Township for the carrying on of a
business, profession or occupation.
   LICENSE: The permission granted for the carrying on of a business,
profession or occupation.
   MISDEMEANOR: Any offense for which a sentence to a term of imprisonment in
other than a penitentiary for less than one year may be imposed.
   NUISANCE: Anything offensive or obnoxious to the health and welfare of the
inhabitants of the Township; or any act or thing repugnant to, or creating a
hazard to, or having a detrimental effect on the property of another person or
to the community.
   OCCUPANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such building or land whether alone or with
others.
   OFFENSE: Any act forbidden by any provision of this Code or the omission of
any act required by the provisions of this Code.
   OFFICERS: Whenever reference is made in this Code to a Township officer by
title only, this shall be construed as though followed by the words "of Leyden
Township".
   OPERATOR: The person who is in charge of any operation, business or
profession.
   OWNER: As applied to a building or land, shall include any part owner, joint
owner, tenant in common, joint tenant or lessee of the whole or of a part of
such building or land.
   PERSON: Any natural person, public or private corporation, firm,
partnership, association, organization, government or any other group acting as
a unit, as well as any trustee, receiver, assignee or personal representative
thereof.
   PERSONAL PROPERTY: Shall include every description of money, goods,
chattels, effects, evidence of rights in action and all written instruments by
which any pecuniary obligation, right or title to property is created,
acknowledged, transferred, increased, defeated, discharged or diminished and
every right or interest therein.
   PROPERTY: Includes real and personal property.
   REAL PROPERTY: Includes lands, tenements and hereditaments and shall include
all chattels affixed or annexed to land.
   STATE: The State of Illinois.
   STREET: The entire width between property lines of every way or place open
to the use of the public for purposes of vehicular or pedestrian travel
including alleys, lanes, courts, boulevards, public ways, public squares,
public places and sidewalks.
   TENANT: As applied to a building or land, shall include any person who
occupies the whole or any part of such buildings or land, whether alone or with
others.
   TOWNSHIP or TOWN: Leyden Township, County of Cook, State of Illinois. (1992
Code)
1-3-3: INTENT:
   All general provisions, terms, phrases and expressions contained in this
Code shall be liberally construed in order that the true intent of the Town
Board may be carried out. (1992 Code)
1-3-4: CATCHLINES:
   The catchlines of the several sections of the Town Code are intended as mere
catchwords to indicate the content of the section and shall not be deemed or
taken to be titles of such sections, nor be deemed to govern, limit, modify or
in any manner affect the scope, meaning or intent of the provisions of any
division or section hereof, nor unless expressly so provided, shall they be so
deemed when any of such sections, including the catchlines, are amended or re-
enacted. (1992 Code)
CHAPTER 4
GENERAL PENALTY
SECTION:
1-4-1: General Penalty
1-4-2: Application Of Provisions
1-4-3: Liability Of Officers And Employees; Indemnification
1-4-1: GENERAL PENALTY:
   Any person convicted of a violation of any section or provision of this
Code, where no other penalty is set forth, shall be punished by a fine not less
than seventy five dollars ($75.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars
($750.00) for each offense. (Ord. TO-2019-1, 1-8-2019)
1-4-2: APPLICATION OF PROVISIONS:
   A.   The penalty provided in this chapter shall be applicable to every
section of this Code the same as though it were a part of each and every
separate section unless otherwise indicated. Any person convicted of a
violation of any section of this Code where a duty is prescribed or obligation
imposed, or where any action which is of a continuing nature is forbidden or is
declared to be unlawful, shall be deemed guilty of a petty offense unless
otherwise indicated. A separate offense shall be deemed committed upon each day
such duty or obligation remains unperformed or such act continues, unless
otherwise specifically provided in this Code.
   B.   In all cases where the same offense is made punishable or is created by
different clauses or sections of this Code, the prosecuting officer may elect
under which to proceed; but not more than one recovery shall be had against the
same person for the same offense; provided, that the revocation of a license or
permit shall not be considered a recovery or penalty so as to bar any other
penalty being enforced.
   C.   Whenever the doing of any act or the omission to do any act constitutes
a breach of any section or provision of this Code and there shall be no fine or
penalty specifically declared for such breach, the provisions of this chapter
shall apply. (1992 Code)
1-4-3: LIABILITY OF OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES; INDEMNIFICATION:
   A.   Liability: No provision of this Code designating the duties of any
officer or employee shall be so construed as to make such officer or employee
liable for any fine or penalty provided for a failure to perform such duty,
unless the intention of the Town Board of Trustees to impose such fine or
penalty on such officer or employee is specifically and clearly expressed in
the section creating the duty.
   B.   Insurance: To the extent authorized by law, the Board may purchase
insurance indemnifying its officers, employees or agents against loss or
liability resulting from their alleged wrongful or negligent acts while acting
within the scope of their official duties and functions, including wrongful or
negligent acts while discharging or engaging in official duties and functions,
and wrongful or negligent omissions or failures to act within the scope of
their official duties and functions.
   C.   Defense And Indemnification:
      1.   If any claim or action is instituted against a present or former
officer, employee or agent of the Town based on an injury arising out of an act
or omission occurring within the scope of such person’s official duties or
functions, such person shall immediately report the claim or action to the Town
Supervisor, and to the Board in the case of claims or actions against the
Supervisor.
      2.   In the event that a claim or action is instituted against an
officer, employee or agent of the Town which is based on an injury arising out
of an act or omission occurring within the scope of their official duties or
functions, except where the injury results from intentional or wilful
misconduct, the Town shall through its insurance carrier or independently if
there is not insurance coverage:
         a.   Appear and defend against the claim or action.
         b.   Pay or indemnify the officer, agent or employee for court costs
incurred in the defense of such claim or action.
         c.   Pay or indemnify the officer, agent or employee for a judgment
based on such claim or action.
         d.   Pay or indemnify the officer, agent or employee for a compromise
or settlement of such claim or action.
      3.   All present or former officers, employees or agents are required to
cooperate fully with the Town, its insurance carrier and its officers, agents
or employees in the defense of any such claim or action. The Town’s obligation
to defend and/or indemnify is specifically conditioned upon such good faith
cooperation.
      4.   The Town shall have no duty to independently defend or indemnify the
persons described above to the extent that insurance coverage is available to
defend and indemnify such present or former officers, agents or employees.
Nothing contained herein is intended or shall be construed to waive, release or
modify any rights or claims which the Town may have under any policies of
insurance now or hereafter obtained by the Town or to create or confer any
rights, benefits, claims or actions upon persons who had, have or may have
claims against the Town or its officers, agents or employees.
      5.   It is intended that the officers, agents or employees of the Town
shall be provided with a defense against and indemnification for all claims or
actions which may now or hereafter be asserted or instituted against them for
actions or omissions occurring within the scope of their official duties or
functions, but only to the extent not inconsistent with the statutes or public
policy of the State. To the extent insurance coverage is unavailable, the Town
may decline to defend and indemnify present or former officers, agents or
employees against claims or actions based on reckless, wilful or intentional
violations of clearly established duties or rights; however, the Town shall, to
the extent insurance coverage is unavailable, indemnify such persons for their
court costs in successfully defending such claims or actions.
      6.   Nothing contained herein is intended or shall be construed to waive,
relinquish, modify or release any rights of contribution, indemnity or
subrogation which the Town may have. (1992 Code; amd. Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-
2022)
CHAPTER 5
TOWN BOARD OF TRUSTEES
SECTION:
1-5-1: Meetings Of The Town Board
1-5-2: Special Meetings
1-5-3: Chair
1-5-4: Proceedings Before The Town Board
1-5-5: Officers And Employees
1-5-6: Personnel Policies
1-5-1: MEETINGS OF THE TOWN BOARD:
The Town Board of Trustees may meet for the purpose of discussing public
business at such times and places as may be determined by the Board from time
to time.
   A.   Regular meetings of the Town Board of Trustees shall be held on the
second Tuesday of each month at six o’clock (6:00) P.M. for discussing and
conducting all public business.
   B.   Any regular or financial meetings of the Town Board of Trustees may be
adjourned to a later date. Any subject may be considered at an adjourned
meeting that might have been discussed at the original meeting.
   C.   Financial meetings of the Town Board of Trustees shall be held on the
second Tuesday of each month at five thirty o’clock (5:30) P.M. for the purpose
of approving bills and payables and for discussing public business concerning
the expenditures of public funds.
   D.   If the regular meeting of the Town Board of Trustees falls on a legal
holiday, the regular meeting shall be held on the next Tuesday that is not a
legal holiday. (Ord. TO-95-1, 3-28-1995; amd. Ord. TO-2021-4, 6-24-2021; Ord.
TO-2022-15, 10-11-2022)
1-5-2: SPECIAL MEETINGS:
   Upon request of the Supervisor or any two (2) members of the Board, the Town
Clerk shall call a special meeting of the Town Board at the time requested and
shall furnish to the members of the Board at least forty eight (48) hours'
notice thereof. The Town Clerk shall also give public notice of any special
meeting at least twenty four (24) hours before such meeting, which notice shall
also include the agenda for the meeting, by posting a copy of the notice at the
Town Hall. The Town Clerk shall also give notice to any news medium which has
filed an annual request for notice of the Town's meetings in the same manner in
which members of the Town Board were notified of the meeting. In the event of a
bona fide emergency, notice of an emergency special meeting shall be given as
soon as practicable to any news medium which has filed an annual request for
notice, but in no event later than the time at which the meeting is scheduled
to begin. (1992 Code)
1-5-3: CHAIR:
   The Supervisor shall be the Chair of the Board and shall preside at all
regular and special meetings of the Town Board. In the absence of the
Supervisor, the Town Clerk shall call for a motion to appoint a Chair Pro Tem
and shall record the vote of all Trustees. The Chair Pro Tem shall preside at
such regular or special meeting in the absence of the Supervisor. (1992 Code;
amd. Ord. TO-2022-15, 10-11-2022)
1-5-4: PROCEEDINGS BEFORE THE TOWN BOARD:
   Robert’s Rules of Order shall govern the proceedings of the Town Board where
applicable and when not in conflict with federal or Illinois statutes or this
Code; provided, however, the Town Board may adopt rules of order revising,
repealing, amending, suspending, supplementing or supplanting, in whole or in
part, Robert’s Rules of Order.
   A.   Public Participation Rules at Meetings of the Town Board:
      1.   Purpose. The Town Board encourages public participation at its
meetings. All regular and special meetings are conducted in compliance with the
Illinois Open Meetings Act, and are therefore open for public observation.
Pursuant to Sections 2.05 and 2.06(g) of the Illinois Open Meetings Act (5 ILCS
120/2.05 and 120/2.06(g), respectively), the Town Board establishes the
following Rules to govern public comment and recording of meetings during
regular and special Board meetings.
      2.   Rules:
         a.   Public comments are permitted during the Public Comments segments
of regular and special Board meetings as noted on the agendas of such meetings.
         b.   Public comments shall be limited to a total of five (5) minutes
per person unless the Supervisor grants additional time as needed and within
reasonable time limits.
         c.   Persons wishing to speak must be present at the meeting. Public
comment by use of any telecommunication device, unless otherwise provided by
the Illinois Open Meetings Act, will not be permitted except in the case of
individuals with disabilities that prevent them from attending in person.
Individuals who cannot attend due to disability or who require disability
related accommodations to allow them to observe and/or participate are
requested to contact the Town Clerk in advance, if possible, to allow the
Township to arrange reasonable accommodations, if feasible.
         d.   If a group with similar views on an issue wishes to speak during
the public comment period, the Board requests that a spokesperson be selected
to address the Board. Redundancy and repetition does not facilitate an orderly
and efficient meeting. If additional matters are to be presented by any other
members of the group, the Supervisor may limit the number of such persons and
limit the presentation to information not already presented by the group’s
spokesperson.
         e.   At the beginning of the Public Comments segment of the meeting,
the Supervisor will ask if anyone wishes to address the Board and will
determine the order in which speakers will be recognized. No person shall
address the Board without first being recognized by the Supervisor.
         f.   Each person desiring to address the Board shall first state his/
her name for the record, state the subject, and state whom he/she is
representing if he/she represents an organization or other persons.
         g.   An individual will not be allowed to speak a second time until
the Board has heard from all members of the public who wish to speak and only
upon the majority vote of the Board.
         h.   Public comments must pertain to an item on the agenda or to an
issue/matter relating to the Township. The Supervisor retains the right to stop
any speaker who raises issues that are not on the agenda or are not germane to
the Township.
         i.   Public comment is not intended to require Board members or
Township staff to provide any answer to the speaker. Discussions between
speakers and members of the audience will not be allowed. The Board will not
necessarily respond to comment provided at the public meeting at the same time
comment is given. Consideration will be given to the public comment and further
research may be required before the Board takes any action regarding the public
comment. Although questions may be asked of a Board member or a member of the
Township’s staff, those individuals may decline to answer when a complete
answer requires research or deliberate consideration.
         j.   Comments shall be presented in a respectful manner, and
participants shall conduct themselves in an orderly and civil manner which
displays mutual respect. Use of profanity, inappropriate language, innuendos,
or other offensive actions and gestures shall not be permitted.
         k.   Public comments are not a forum to be used by political
candidates to advance their candidacy for any public office.
         l.   The Board reserves the right to remove anyone who becomes
hostile, argumentative, threatens the public’s or an individual’s safety or is
disruptive to the meeting. If the party being asked to leave does not
voluntarily leave or cease the behavior, law enforcement will be called to
remove the person.
         m.   Questions regarding specific elected officials, officers, agents
or employees of the Township will not be entertained. Questions of this type
may be addressed, in writing, to the Supervisor, who shall determine the
appropriate method of response.
         n.   Members of the audience will not engage in conversation while the
meeting of the Town Board is in session.
         o.   Members of the audience will not be permitted free movement about
the meeting room while the meeting of the Town Board is in session. Members of
the audience may enter and leave the board room at any time, provided such
entrance or exit is made quietly and in an orderly fashion.
         p.   Individuals who appear to be visibly intoxicated shall not be
allowed to attend a Town Board meeting or address the Town Board.
         q.   The consumption of any solid or liquid food or the smoking of any
tobacco product or consumption of cannabis is prohibited at any meeting of the
Town Board.
   B.   Recording Meetings:
      1.   Cameras. Cameras, including still cameras, move cameras, and
television cameras, using flashlights or lighting equipment other than the
normal light furnished in the board room, will not be allowed while meetings of
the Town Board are in session unless otherwise permitted by the Supervisor.
      2.   Battery operated recording equipment is permitted, provided the
operation thereof is silent. The microphone or pick up shall not be placed in
the section of the board room designated for the Town Board unless otherwise
permitted by the Supervisor.
      3.   No equipment may be set up or used in any manner so as to obstruct
the view of any person in the audience.
   C.   The Supervisor or his/her designee shall be responsible for the
enforcement of the provisions of this Section and shall be empowered to
reprimand and/or eject any and all persons violating the provisions of this
Section. (1992 Code; amd. Ord. 2019-5, 5-14-2019; Ord. TO-2022-7, 5-10-2022)
1-5-5: OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES:
   In accordance with chapter 6 of this title and as provided by law, the board
may create, eliminate, consolidate or combine the offices, positions,
departments or units of the administrative and executive departments of the
town. (1992 Code)
1-5-6: PERSONNEL POLICIES:
   The board may adopt, amend or repeal such employment policies or guidelines
as it may deem appropriate to promote efficiency and economy in operation of
the township government and to maintain and stimulate high morale among
township employees. However, such policies or guidelines are a statement of
current intent only and, unless expressly provided otherwise, shall not be
construed as creating any contractual employment rights. (1992 Code)
CHAPTER 6
TOWNSHIP OFFICERS AND EMPLOYEES
SECTION:
1-6-1: Town Supervisor
1-6-2: Township Administrator
1-6-3: Township Attorney
1-6-4: Township Engineer
1-6-5: Other Professionals
1-6-6: Salaries Of Officers
1-6-7: Township Clerk
1-6-8: Deputy Clerk
1-6-1: TOWN SUPERVISOR:
   A.   Bond Requirements: The Town Supervisor shall give bond to the Town in
such amount and with such sureties as is provided by law.
   B.   Chief Executive Officer: The Town Supervisor is the Chief Executive
Officer of the Town as provided by law and is authorized and empowered to:
      1.   Enforce all laws and ordinances of the Town.
      2.   Recommend to the Board such measures that the Town Supervisor deems
to be in the best interest of the Town.
      3.   Exercise control of all administrative departments and divisions of
the Town (excepting the Highway Department and the assessor’s office) now in
existence or that may hereafter be created by the Board.
      4.   Make recommendations to the Board concerning compensation for each
appointive office or position in the Town.
      5.   Make recommendations to the Board concerning the creation,
elimination, consolidation or combination of offices, positions, depart ments
or units of the administrative and executive department of the Town.
      6.   Subject to prior appropriation of the Board, appoint, suspend,
remove or transfer officers and employees of the Town based upon the merit and
fitness of such officer or employee.
      7.   Serve as Purchasing Agent for the Town if no Township Administrator
is appointed and acting.
      8.   Perform such other lawful duties as may be provided by law. (1992
Code; amd. Ord. TO-2022-11, 8-9-2022; Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022)
1-6-2: TOWNSHIP ADMINISTRATOR:
   A.   Office Created: The office of Township Administrator is hereby created,
subject to the provisions of this section. The Township Administrator, under
the direction of the Township Supervisor, serves as the Chief Administrative
Officer of the Township.
   B.   Qualifications Of Township Administrator: The Township Administrator
shall be chosen by the Township Supervisor and Leyden Town Board ("Town Board")
solely on the basis of executive and administrative qualifications with special
reference to specific professional education for, actual experience in, and
knowledge of, accepted practices in respect to the administration of local
government and the duties of the office as specified in subsection E, below.
   C.   Appointment And Relationship To Elected Officials: The Township
Administrator shall be appointed by the Township Supervisor, with the advice
and consent of a majority vote of the Town Board, for a term of employment
which shall not exceed the term of office of the Township Supervisor and
Township Board of Trustees. The Township Administrator shall, at all times, be
subject to the authority and direction of the Township Supervisor and Town
Board.
   D.   Compensation: The rate of compensation of the Township Administrator
shall be set by the Town Board and may be adjusted from time to time as the
Board deems appropriate.
   E.   Removal From Office: The Township Administrator shall, at all times, be
subject to removal from office by a majority vote of the Town Board.
   F.   Powers And Duties: The Township Administrator shall be responsible for
the proper administration of all affairs of the Township and for planning and
developing Township programs, policies and activities. In discharging these
responsibilities, the Township Administrator shall:
      1.   Direct, supervise, evaluate and coordinate the administration of all
departments, staff, and programs of the Township and make recommendations on
staffing requirements, except as otherwise provided by law.
      2.   Appoint, and when necessary for the effective execution of Township
services, suspend or remove any employee and appointive officer, except as
otherwise provided by law, subject to applicable ordinances and/or policies
adopted by the Town Board. All appointments and removals shall be based solely
upon merit and the qualifications or disqualifications of the individual
involved, without regard to race, religion, color, age, sex, national origin,
ancestry, order of protection status, marital status, disability, military
status, sexual orientation, pregnancy, unfavorable discharge from military
service, or conviction record, or as otherwise in violation of any applicable
federal or state law.
      3.   Recommend appointment, and when necessary for the effective
execution of Township services, suspension or removal, of any department head
to the Town Board, except when otherwise provided by law. All recommended
appointments and removals shall be based solely upon merit and the
qualifications or disqualifications of the individual involved, without regard
to race, religion, color, age, sex, national origin, ancestry, order of
protection status, marital status, disability, military status, sexual
orientation, pregnancy, unfavorable discharge from military service, or
conviction record, or as otherwise in violation of any applicable federal or
state law.
      4.   Attend all Town Board meetings. The Township Administrator shall
have the right to take part in all discussions, unless otherwise directed by a
majority vote of the Town Code; but shall not vote.
      5.   Provide for the enforcement of all Township laws, ordinances and
policies within the Township, subject to applicable federal, state and county
laws.
      6.   Subject to the applicable provisions of the Township Code and
Illinois Municipal Budget Law, serve as the Township Budget Officer, and
prepare and submit to the Town Board, in coordination with the Township
Supervisor and the Highway Commissioner, a recommended annual budget for
Township operations, property tax levy, and capital improvement programs. When
the annual budget or the capital improvement program(s) have been approved by
the Town Board, the Township Administrator shall be responsible for the
administration of said budget and capital improvement program(s).
      7.   Prepare and submit written reports to the Town Board at the monthly
Town Board meeting, and as the Town Board may require, concerning the
administrative activities and operations of Township departments, offices and
agencies.
      8.   Advise the Town Board on a regular basis, or as requested by the
Board, of the present financial condition and future needs of the Township.
      9.   Advise the Town Board on pending public policy proposals and
recommend to the Town Board the adoption of such measures as the Township
Administrator may deem necessary or expedient for the health, safety and
welfare of the community or the improvement of administrative services.
      10.   Be responsible for the procurement of commodities and services for
all Township departments, offices and agencies, and promulgate purchasing rules
and regulations to be followed by Township employees in the procurement of
goods and services.
      11.   Propose to the Town Board personnel rules, regulations and policies
as required by state and federal law and as the Township Administrator deems
necessary to manage the personnel policies of the Township.
      12.   Responsible for researching, initiating action for, applying for
and supervising the implementation of funding grants from various sources for
the improvement and development of Township capital improvement projects, as
well as for services to the Township and its residents.
      13.   Keep Township staff fully informed of all policies and decisions of
the Township Board, as well as other Township activities, by holding monthly
staff meetings and as needed.
      14.   Act as intermediary/liaison between various Township boards,
commissions, committees, agencies and departments and their professional
advisors to facilitate communication with the local government framework.
      15.   Establish a long-term plan in conjunction with the Township Board
to meet the changing governmental needs of Township citizens.
      16.   Provide administrative support to the Highway Commissioner and
assist the Highway Commissioner in the preparation of the annual road and
budget and property tax levy.
      17.   Perform such other duties as may be required by law or Township
ordinance or as may, from time to time, be requested by the Township
Supervisor, Highway Commissioner or Town Board.
   G.   Acting Township Administrator: If, because of temporary absence,
disability or illness, the Township Administrator is unable to carry out the
functions of this office, the Township Supervisor may appoint an individual to
serve as Acting Township Administrator to carry out the duties of the Township
Administrator during the Township Administrator's absence.
   H.   Authority Of Elected Officials: Nothing in this section shall be deemed
to diminish or detract from the statutory powers and authority of the
Township's elected officials and Town Board.
   I.   At-Will Employee: Nothing herein shall be construed as changing the
"at-will" status of any Township employee, including but not limited to the
Township Administrator. (Ord. TO-2021-5, 6-24-2021)
1-6-3: TOWNSHIP ATTORNEY:
   The Board may employ and fix the compensation of a Township Attorney to
advise the Board and serve as attorney for the Town. The Board may engage
additional counsel whenever in its opinion additional counsel is necessary.
(1992 Code)
1-6-4: TOWNSHIP ENGINEER:
   The Board may employ and fix the compensation of an Illinois registered
professional engineer to provide professional engineering services for the
Town. The Board may employ additional engineers whenever in its opinion
additional engineers are necessary. (1992 Code)
1-6-5: OTHER PROFESSIONALS:
   Whenever it is necessary in the board's opinion to employ individuals
possessing a high degree of professional skill where the ability or fitness of
the individual plays an important part, the board may contract for such
services without competitive bidding. (1992 Code)
1-6-6: SALARIES OF OFFICERS:
   A.   Township Supervisor: The salary and compensation of the supervisor,
whose term of office will commence on or after the third Monday of May, 2021,
is established as follows:
      1.   An annual salary of twenty thousand dollars ($20,000.00) for
services as township supervisor, as the treasurer of the township road district
and as the ex-officio supervisor of general assistance, payable from the
following funds:
         a.   General town fund: Five thousand dollars ($5,000.00).
         b.   Road and bridge fund: Five thousand dollars ($5,000.00)
(inclusive of the $1,000.00 statutory stipend for serving as treasurer of the
road district).
         c.   Sewer and water fund: Seven thousand dollars ($7,000.00).
         d.   General assistance fund: Three thousand dollars ($3,000.00).
   B.   Township Trustees: The salary and compensation of each township
trustee, whose term of office will commence on or after the third Monday of
May, 2021, is established as follows:
      1.   An annual salary of twelve thousand dollars ($12,000.00) for
services as a township trustee.
   C.   Town Clerk: The salary and compensation of the town clerk, whose term
of office will commence on or after the third Monday of May, 2021, is
established as follows:
      1.   An annual salary of sixty-eight thousand dollars ($68,000.00) for
services as the town clerk.
      2.   Health, hospitalization and accident insurance benefits based upon
established township policy.
      3.   Membership in the Illinois municipal retirement fund and the
benefits pertaining thereto as provided by law.
   D.   Township Highway Commissioner: The salary and compensation of the
highway commissioner, whose term of office will commence on or after the third
Monday of May, 2021, is established as follows:
      1.   An annual salary of twenty thousand dollars ($20,000.00) for
services as the township highway commissioner with one-half (½) to be paid from
the general town fund and one-half (½) to be paid from the road and bridge
fund.
   E.   Township Assessor: The annual salary and compensation of the township
assessor, whose term of office will commence on January 1, 2022, is established
as follows:
      1.   An annual salary of thirty one thousand dollars ($31,000.00) for
services as the township assessor.
      2.   Health, hospitalization and accident insurance benefits based upon
established township policy.
      3.   Membership in the Illinois municipal retirement fund and the
