Township except from a residential premises owned or occupied by the individual
conducting the garage sale.
   B.   A garage sale license under this Chapter is not required for any garage
sale conducted within the corporate limits of a city or village within Leyden
Township that regulates garage sales. (Ord. TO-99-8, 6-8-1999)
2-2-3: PERMITTED LOCATIONS FOR DEALING IN SECONDHAND ARTICLES:
   A.   It shall be unlawful to conduct the business of dealing in secondhand
property in the Township except from premises for which dealing in secondhand
property is a permitted retail business use under the Cook County Zoning
Ordinance, for which a special use permit has been issued under the Cook County
Zoning Ordinance for dealing in secondhand property as a retail business use.
   B.   An estate sale may be conducted by a business that regularly conducts
estate sales as a business entity.
   C.   A garage sale license under this Chapter is not required for any garage
sale conducted within the corporate limits of a city or village within Leyden
Township that regulates garage sales. (Ord. TO-99-8, 6-8-1999; amd. Ord. 2019-
7, 5-14-2019)
2-2-4: GARAGE SALE LICENSE REQUIRED:
   It shall be unlawful for any person to conduct or to allow the conducting of
a garage sale on the person’s premises without having applied for and received
from the township clerk a license to conduct such sale. Each license shall be
prominently displayed on the residence or garage covered by the license in such
a manner that it is easily visible to persons passing by the premises. (Ord.
TO-99-8, 6-8-1999; amd. Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022)
2-2-5: LICENSE FEE:
   A license fee of ten dollars ($10.00) shall be charged for each license
issued. (Ord. TO-2012-4, 3-13-2012; amd. Ord. 2019-7, 5-14-2019; Ord. TO-2021-
9, 9-14-2021; Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-2-6: LIMIT ON LENGTH AND FREQUENCY OF GARAGE SALES:
   Licenses for garage sales shall be valid for not more than two (2)
consecutive days, between the hours of nine o'clock (9:00) A.M. and five
o'clock (5:00) P.M. No more than two (2) garage sales shall be conducted or
permitted on the same premises within a calendar year. (Ord. TO-99-8, 6-8-1999)
2-2-7: MAINTENANCE OF ORDER; COMPLIANCE WITH OTHER LAWS:
   The individual conducting the garage sale and the owner or tenant of the
premises on which such sale or activity is conducted shall maintain the
premises in a neat, clean and presentable condition before, during and after
such sale. In the event good order is not maintained, or the sale is conducted
in violation of any of the provisions of this chapter, such individual(s) shall
be subject to the penalties provided in
2-2-9 of this chapter.
   All persons conducting garage sales shall comply with all other applicable
federal, state and local laws, including zoning and traffic laws. (Ord. TO-99-
8, 6-8-1999)
2-2-8: SIGNS; OTHER ITEMS PROHIBITED:
   A.   On-Sale Signage: Only one sign shall be permitted on the premises where
the garage sale is taking place, unless such property has frontage on two (2)
public streets, in which case two (2) signs are permitted, one at each
frontage. Each sign shall not exceed six (6) square feet in area, shall not
exceed a height of four feet (4'), and shall not be located on any portion of
the township's right of way. Such signs shall not be erected more than twenty
four (24) hours prior to the permitted start of the garage sale. Such signs
shall be removed within two (2) hours after the completion of the sale but in
no event no later than seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. on the day the license
expires.
   B.   Off-Site Directional Signage: Three (3) temporary directional signs may
be permitted on the public right-of-way. Each sign shall not exceed six (6)
square feet in area, shall not exceed a height of three feet (3'), shall not be
placed within five feet (5') of the paved portion of the township's right-of-
way, and shall only be erected during the permitted hours of the garage sale as
stated on the license. No signs (other than the 3 permitted in this
subsection), banners, balloons, flags, streamers or other advertising devices
shall be erected or placed in the public right-of-way or affixed to a utility
pole, street sign, traffic control sign or any other structure, wire, cable or
other device located on, over or above any public right-of-way, street or road.
   C.   Garage sale signs shall not be displayed on or within vehicles, or be
placed in a location, or in a manner which would cause an obstruction to the
clear view of traffic or pose a hazard. Any other advertising devices intended
to draw attention to this sale, including, but not limited to, banners,
balloons, flags, streamers, and loudspeakers, are prohibited.
   D.   Garage sale signage must display the address (house number and street
name) of the location for the garage sale and the garage sale permit number.
   E.   The individual conducting the garage sale and the owner or tenant of
the premises on which such sale or activity is conducted shall not suffer or
permit any garage sale signs, banners, balloons, flags, streamers or other such
device to be posted or erected in violation of this section, and they shall
immediately remove any such signs posted or erected in violation of this
section. (Ord. TO-2010-5, 4-13-2010; amd. Ord. 2019-7, 5-14-2019)
2-2-9: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
   Any person who violates any of the provisions of this chapter shall be fined
not less than thirty dollars ($30.00) nor more than three hundred dollars
($300.00) for each offense. Each day a violation is found to exist shall
constitute a separate offense. The owner of the property for which a garage
sale license is obtained shall be responsible for all posting of all
advertising devices relating to such garage sale and shall be responsible for
any unlawful posting. (Ord. TO-2010-5, 4-13-2010)
CHAPTER 3
COMMERCIAL FILM PRODUCTION
SECTION:
2-3-1: Purpose And Intent
2-3-2: Definitions
2-3-3: Permit Required
2-3-4: Exceptions
2-3-5: Deadline For Filing Applications
2-3-6: Permit Application
2-3-7: Processing Permit Applications
2-3-8: Permit Approval/Denial
2-3-9: Permit Conditions
2-3-10: Fees/Charges
2-3-11: Duties Of Permittee
2-3-12: Pyrotechnics
2-3-13: Permit Revocation/Suspension
2-3-14: Appeals
2-3-15: Permit Duration And Extensions
2-3-16: Hours Of Production
2-3-17: Vehicle And Equipment Parking
2-3-18: Violations And Penalties
2-3-1: PURPOSE AND INTENT:
   It is the purpose of this chapter to provide specific rules governing the
audio recording and/or the filming or taping of movies, TV programs,
commercials or training films, and related activities on locations within the
unincorporated areas of Leyden Township. This chapter is intended to ensure
that filming/taping/recording is done consistent with public health and safety
and the protection of property so as to:
   A.   Provide for adequate protection for the personal and property rights of
affected residents, schools and businesses;
   B.   Provide for pedestrian and driving safety and convenience;
   C.   Prevent unreasonable interference with the flow of pedestrian or
vehicle traffic, including ingress to or egress from any residence, school or
place of business, or from the street to the sidewalk, by persons exiting or
entering parked or standing vehicles and to generally protect the rights of the
public to the safe and normal use of the public streets, rights-of-way and
property;
   D.   Maintain and protect the value of surrounding properties;
   E.   Reduce exposure of the Township to personal injury and/or property
damage, claims and litigation;
   F.   Streamline the audio and/or film permit process and facilitate issuance
of a permit for audio and/or film production activities;
   G.   Ensure the public health, safety and welfare and to avoid unreasonable
and unnecessary disruptions to the community;
   H.   Establish standards and procedures for evaluating requests for audio
and/or film production permits;
   I.   Assure that requests for audio and/or film production permits are
evaluated on a case-by-case basis so as to recognize that each permit
application presents a unique set of circumstances; and
   J.   Assure that the Township will be adequately compensated both for the
direct use of Township resources and for the effects on Township resources and
operations arising from audio and/or film production activities through a
permit application process. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019)
2-3-2: DEFINITIONS:
   For the purposes of this chapter, the following words and phrases shall have
the meanings given in this section, unless the context clearly requires a
different meaning:
   APPLICANT: The person, organization, corporation, association or other
entity applying for a permit to audio record or film in the unincorporated
areas of Leyden Township.
   AUDIO AND FILM PRODUCTION: The process of recording live action on film,
digital recording, magnetic tape or any other medium, for later commercial sale
or distribution as a movie, television show, radio show, music video,
advertising commercial, training film or educational program.
   AUDIO RECORDING AND FILM PRODUCTION ACTIVITY: Any and all activities related
to audio recording and film production, including, but not limited to the
staging, set-up, shooting, site restoration, using audio and film production
equipment, gatherings of persons involved in the audio and film production,
filming, recording, videotaping, photographing, or other similar process
conducted for the making of still photographs, motion pictures, television
programs, video games, commercial and nontheatrical audio and film productions.
   AUDIO RECORDING AND FILM PRODUCTION ACTIVITY CHARGES: The charges
established by the Township to compensate the Township both for the direct use
of Township resources and for the effects on Township resources and operations
arising from audio and film production activities pursuant to an audio and/or
film production permit.
   AUDIO RECORDING AND FILM PRODUCTION EQUIPMENT: Any object used in audio and
film production, including but not limited to lighting equipment, sound
equipment, cameras, dressing rooms, trailers, props, furnishings and vehicles.
   AUDIO RECORDING AND FILM PRODUCTION PERMIT: A permit issued in accordance
with the procedures and provisions of this chapter.
   ISSUING AUTHORITY: The Township Supervisor and duly authorized designee.
   NEWS PURPOSE: An audio and/or film production activity conducted for the
purpose of reporting on persons, events, or scenes which are in the news for
newspapers, television news and other news media.
   PERMITTEE: The person, organization, corporation, association or other
entity issued an audio or film production permit.
   PRIVATE PROPERTY: Any property not owned by Leyden Township, and on which
filming would not interfere with public rights-of-way, access or safety.
   PUBLIC STREET: Any street or road maintained by Leyden Township and located
within the unincorporated areas of the Township.
   STUDENT FILM: The staging, shooting, making, capturing, taking or recording
of images for purposes resulting from enrollment in or in connection with high
school, junior college, college, university, specialty education institutions
such as trade schools, film schools or art schools or any other educational
program.
   STUDIO: A fixed place of business where audio and/or filming activities are
regularly conducted upon the premises.
   TOWNSHIP: The Town of Leyden/Leyden Township as a governmental corporation
and existing pursuant to the laws of the State of Illinois.
   TOWNSHIP RESOURCES: Township resources means and includes any and all of the
following: a) elected and appointed Township officials; b) Township employees
and personnel; c) operating and administrative departments of the Township; d)
vehicles, equipment, personal property and real estate owned, leased or
operated by or on behalf of the Township; e) streets, sidewalks, parkways,
parking lots, and public rights-of-way located within the Township; and f)
services provided by, on behalf of or under the auspices of the Township,
regardless of the nature of the services, and regardless of whether or not such
services are provided or made available to the citizens, schools and businesses
located in the Township. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-
2022; Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-3: PERMIT REQUIRED:
   Except as provided in section
2-3-4 of this chapter, no person shall engage in, participate in or start any
audio recording or film production activity anywhere within the unincorporated
areas of the Township without first applying and obtaining an audio recording
permit or film production permit from the Township Supervisor in accordance
with the procedures established in this chapter. This permit must be in the
possession of the permittee at all times while on location in the
unincorporated areas of the Township.
   This permit does not constitute or grant permission to use or occupy
property not owned, leased or controlled by the Township. An applicant for a
permit shall obtain the private property’s written permission, consent, and/or
lease for use of the property not owned or controlled by the Township as a
condition for obtaining an audio recording permit or film production permit.
(Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-4: EXCEPTIONS:
   The provisions of this chapter shall not apply to any of the following
activities provided that the activity will not require the closure of a public
street, or substantially impede traffic thereon:
   A.   Audio or film production activities conducted for news purposes;
   B.   Audio or film production activities conducted at studios;
   C.   Audio or film production activities conducted for use in a criminal
investigation or Civil or Criminal Court proceeding;
   D.   Audio or film production activities conducted for student films as
defined in
2-3-2 of this chapter or at an adult education program conducted under the
auspices of a school district, park district, or community organization that is
either located in Leyden Township or is supported by taxes paid in whole or in
part by residents of Leyden Township;
   E.   Noncommercial audio recording or filming activities conducted solely
for private or family use; or
   F.   Audio or filming production activities conducted by or for Leyden
Township. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019)
2-3-5: DEADLINE FOR FILING APPLICATIONS:
   Applications for an audio production permit or film production permit must
be filed with the Township Clerk not less than fifteen (15) business days prior
to the date the audio production activity or film production activity is to
begin on a form furnished by the Township. No late applications will be
processed by the Township unless the Township Supervisor determines that
special circumstances exist relative to the application which would have
precluded its application on a timely basis. Upon a showing of good cause, the
Township Supervisor shall consider applications which are filed after the
filing deadline if there is sufficient time to process and investigate the
application, and for Township staff to prepare for the audio and/or filming
production activity. An additional fee may be imposed for applications filed
less than fifteen (15) business days prior to the audio or film production
activity. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-6: PERMIT APPLICATION:
   The permit application shall be on a form furnished by the Township Clerk
and signed by the applicant or authorized agent thereof. No application is
considered submitted unless it is accompanied with the required fee(s) as set
forth in subsection
2-3-10A of this chapter and payment of all outstanding debts owed the Township.
   A.   Contents Of Application: The application shall contain all information
and statements, and shall be accompanied by all documentation required by this
section, plus such other information as may be required by this chapter for the
type of audio or film production activities proposed, and such other
information as the Township Supervisor may reasonably deem necessary to
complete the review of the application.
   B.   Signature Under Oath: The application shall be signed under oath by the
applicant or an authorized representative of the applicant.
   C.   Required Information: The applicant shall provide at least the
following information:
      1.   Type of production (radio, motion picture, television production,
training film, etc.);
      2.   Current name, address and telephone number of applicant and the
production company, if any;
      3.   Name, address, telephone number and an email address of person in
charge of day-to-day operations of the recording and/or film production
(project producer, director, location manager);
      4.   A statement that the person signing the application is authorized to
do so;
      5.   Complete production schedule including dates and times of audio and/
or film production activity and the approximate time when such activity will
begin and end;
      6.   Proposed location(s), including street names, direction, addresses
of location(s), whether public or private, within the unincorporated areas of
the Township where the audio and/or film production activity will take place
and/or for staging and/or storage of audio and/or film production equipment;
      7.   If any of the audio production activity and/or film production
activity is to take place on private property, a letter or statement of
approval, in the form provided in subsection D2 of this section, signed by the
owner(s) and occupant(s) of each private location described pursuant to the
preceding paragraph;
      8.   The description of and approximate number of personnel who will
engage in such activity;
      9.   Description of type of audio and/or film (e.g., commercial, feature
film, film scene, training film, etc.) and description of scenes to be audio
recorded and/or filmed including details of any hazardous activity employing
firearms, explosives, the use of open flame, other pyrotechnical effects,
animals, stunts, filming of moving motor vehicles or aircraft;
      10.   If the audio production activity and/or filming production activity
include special effects which include incendiary or explosive devices, proof of
no less than two million dollars ($2,000,000.00) liability insurance therefor,
along with the name and qualifications of the person in charge of such special
effects, and proof of licensing by the applicable Federal, State and local
agencies. The certificate of insurance shall name Leyden Township as an
additional insured. The insurance required by this subsection shall be in
addition to the general liability insurance coverage required by subsection D3
of this section;
      11.   The proposed name of the film/series, subject matter and primary
actors;
      12.   Description of the types and number of vehicles and equipment to be
on location for the audio and/or film production activities, including, but not
limited to trucks, trailers, buses, limousines and cameras;
      13.   Description of the number of personnel and equipment applicant
proposes to have on the audio and/or film production and staging location(s) to
provide emergency medical treatment for persons involved in the audio and/or
film production activity;
      14.   Description of the types and number of vehicles which will be
parked on public streets, and description of any equipment to be placed on
public property;
      15.   Description of the method and procedures to be used for food
service and health and sanitation on the audio and/or film production location
(s) whether located in unincorporated Leyden Township or within a neighboring
municipality;
      16.   Description of the method and procedures for the removal of garbage
and other waste from the audio and/or film production location(s);
      17.   Description of the types of Township services/resources applicant
anticipates using, such as water, electricity, map cooperation, recycling,
garbage collection and disposal, lighting, Township personnel, property and/or
rights-of-way;
      18.   Evidence of adequate insurance certification as set forth in
subsections C10 and D3 of this section;
      19.   An agreement to pay the Township for all Township audio and film
production activity charges;
      20.   An agreement to pay in full, promptly upon receipt of an invoice,
the cost of repair for any and all damage to public property of any kind,
resulting from or in connection with, the audio and/or film production, and to
restore such property to the condition it was in immediately prior to the audio
and/or film production;
      21.   Hold Harmless Agreement;
      22.   Other information as deemed necessary by the Township Supervisor;
and
      23.   Draft notification as required in subsection D1 of this section for
the approval of the Township Supervisor.
   D.   Required Attachments: In addition to the information required in
subsection C of this section, the following documents shall be submitted prior
to the issuance of a permit.
      1.   Notification To Neighbors: Upon the Township Supervisor’s approval
of a draft Notification to Neighbors, proof that applicant has initiated
notification to all owners of record and occupants of all property situated
within eight hundred (800) linear feet, in each direction and on both sides of
the street or streets of the location(s) upon which audio recording, filming
and staging is expected to occur, not less than ten (10) business days prior to
the first day of the proposed audio and/or film production schedule. The notice
to owners of record and occupants may be delivered personally or sent by U.S.
mail. Additionally, applicant shall post signs at the location(s) upon which
the audio recording, filming and staging of equipment is expected to occur. The
notices shall be in a form approved by the Township Supervisor and shall
contain a written description of the proposed audio and/or film production,
including the proposed production schedule and the type of audio and/or film
production activities, including, but not limited to, employing firearms,
explosives, the use of open flame, other pyrotechnical effects, animals,
stunts, filming of moving motor vehicles or aircraft and other noise-creating
or hazardous devices which disturb the peace, audio and/or film production
equipment applicant proposes to use and location(s) upon which the audio
recording, filming and staging of equipment is to occur. The notice shall state
that the owner(s) of record and the properties’ occupants may submit any
written comments and objections to the Township Supervisor within five (5) days
from receipt of the notice. The notice shall also clearly state that the audio
and/or film production and staging of equipment will be permitted.
      2.   Property Owner Letter Of Approval: The letter or statement required
by subsection C7 of this section shall state the approval and consent of the
owner(s) and, where applicable, of the lessee(s)/occupant(s) of the property,
to the properties’ use as a location for audio and/or film production or
staging of equipment. The signature(s) on the letter shall be notarized. The
letter of approval shall also contain the following statement:
      I hereby certify that I am the owner of record [or, where applicable, the
occupant] of the property located at [street address], which will be used for
audio and/or film production or staging of production equipment. I hereby waive
any claim against Leyden Township, its elected officials, officers, employees
and agents arising out of or in connection with the issuance of the audio and/
or film production permit and will indemnify and hold harmless Leyden Township
for and from any loss, damage, expense, claims and costs of every nature and
kind, including attorneys’ fees, that I may incur as a result of or in
connection with the audio and/or film production activities pursuant to said
permit.
      3.   Certificate Of Insurance: A certificate of insurance, issued by a
company acceptable to the Township Supervisor and authorized to do business in
the State of Illinois. The certificate of insurance shall be in an amount of
not less than one million dollars ($1,000,000.00) for general liability
coverage, including bodily injury, property damage and automobile liability.
The certificate of insurance shall name Leyden Township as an additional
insured, using language acceptable to the Township Supervisor, and shall
contain a provision prohibiting the cancellation or termination of the policy
without providing at least thirty (30) days’ written notice to the Township.
In addition, if the audio and/or film production includes special effects as
set forth in subsection C10 of this section, a certificate of insurance for no
less than two million dollars ($2,000,000.00), as provided therein.
      4.   Worker’s Compensation And Employer’s Liability Insurance: Proof
acceptable to the Township Supervisor that applicant has provided worker’s
compensation insurance, employer’s liability insurance and all other insurance
required by law to be provided for the employees of applicant.
      5.   Indemnification And Hold Harmless Agreement: An indemnification
agreement whereby applicant agrees to defend and hold the Township, its
officers, employees and agents, harmless from any loss, damage, expense, claim
and cost of every nature and kind whatsoever, including attorney’s fees,
arising out of or in connection with the audio and/or film production
authorized under the permit, including without limitation, applicant’s use of
the public resources specified in the audio and/or film production permit.
(Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-7: PROCESSING PERMIT APPLICATIONS:
   A.   Authority Of Township Supervisor: The Township Supervisor shall review
each audio and/or film production permit application to determine whether the
application is complete and whether the application meets the standards
established by this chapter. The Township Supervisor shall also establish the
applicable audio and/or film production and equipment staging activities fees
as provided in section
2-3-10 of this chapter.
   B.   Review Of Application: In reviewing the application, the Township
Supervisor shall review all documents submitted with the application and all
additional documentation required by the Township Supervisor pursuant to
section
2-3-6 of this chapter.
   C.   Standards Of Review: In reviewing each application, the Township
Supervisor shall consider the totality of the circumstances of the proposed
audio and/or film production, as described in all of the application materials,
as well as all impacts, whether direct or indirect, that the proposed audio
and/or film production activities may have on Township resources and
operations. The review of the application shall include, but not limited to a
consideration of the following factors:
      1.   The nature of the Township resources the Township Supervisor has
determined should be assigned to the audio and/or film production activities;
      2.   The nature of additional Township resources the Township Supervisor
has determined should be assigned to the audio and/or film production
activities;
      3.   The extent to which personal and property rights of residents,
schools and businesses are affected and whether such rights can be adequately
protected;
      4.   The nature and extent of any disruptions to the day-to-day
activities of the Township’s residents, schools and businesses, and whether
such disruptions can be adequately minimized;
      5.   The nature and extent of the impact of the proposed audio and/or
film production activities on the right of the public to the safe and normal
use of the Township’s streets, rights-of-way and public property, and whether
such use can be adequately protected;
      6.   The nature and extent of the impact of the proposed audio and/or
film production activities on the right of the public to the orderly
functioning of local government and to the provision of public services, and
whether such governmental functions and public services can be adequately
provided;
      7.   Whether the public health, safety and welfare can be adequately
protected during the audio and/or film production activities;
      8.   Whether the Township can be adequately compensated both for the
direct use of Township resources in the course of the proposed audio and/or
film production activities and for all other effects or impacts on Township
resources and operations that may arise from the proposed audio and/or film
production activities;
      9.   Consideration of any objections received; and
      10.   The experience of the Township and/or neighboring governmental
entities in prior dealings with applicant.
   D.   Setting Application Processing Fees, Audio Production Activity Charges
And/or Film Production Activity Charges: The permit application review process
shall include setting the audio and/or film production activity charges, as
provided in section
2-3-10 of this chapter. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-
2023)
2-3-8: PERMIT APPROVAL/DENIAL:
   A.   The application shall be approved or denied not less than three (3)
business days of the proposed start date unless the proposed audio and/or film
production activity requires extensive review by other Township departments due
to fire, traffic or public safety or audio and/or film production. The permit
shall be approved by the Township Supervisor unless determined from
consideration of the application or other pertinent information that any of the
following conditions exist:
      1.   The audio and/or film production activities will have substantial
negative impact on any of the standards of review set forth in section
2-3-7 of this chapter;
      2.   The audio and/or film production activities will substantially
disrupt the use of a street at a time when it is usually subject to traffic
congestion, or interfere with the operation of emergency vehicles in the
proposed permit area(s);
      3.   The location(s) of the audio and/or film production activities will
substantially interfere with street maintenance work, or a previously
authorized work permit;
      4.   The proposed permit location is on Township property and the audio
and/or film production activities will substantially interfere with other
previously authorized activities, contracts or safety of the public or
residents while on Township property;
      5.   The proposed permit location is on Township property and the audio
and/or film production activities will substantially interfere with Township
functions or the scheduled maintenance of Township buildings or grounds;
      6.   The audio and/or film production activities create a substantial
risk of injury to persons or damage to property;
      7.   Applicant failed to complete the application or the information
contained in the application is found to be false in any material detail; or
      8.   The Township is in emergency status and/or experiencing a shortage
of qualified staff to adequately process the application and/or staff oversight
of the production schedule; or
      9.   The particular audio and/or film production activity would violate
Federal, State, or local law including licensing or permit requirements.
   B.   When the grounds for permit denial can be corrected by imposing
reasonable permit conditions, the Township may impose such conditions rather
than denying the permit. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-
2023)
2-3-9: PERMIT CONDITIONS:
   A.   If approved, the permit shall contain the following standard
conditions:
      1.   Permittee shall, at its own cost and expense, comply with all
statutes, ordinances, regulations and requirements of all governmental
entities, including Federal, State, County, Township, local or Municipal,
whether now in force or hereinafter enacted.
      2.   The permit shall not be transferred to any other person or entity.
      3.   In addition to the fees and charges set forth in section
2-3-10 of this chapter, permittee shall reimburse the Township for any
additional costs incurred by the Township upon receipt of receiving notice from
the Township of any additional costs.
      4.   Security in all public locations in unincorporated Leyden and on
Leyden Township property shall be by the Cook County Sheriff’s Office. The
number of required Sheriff Officers shall be coordinated and approved by the
Cook County Sheriff’s Office and the Township Supervisor. Permittee shall
contract directly with the Cook County Sheriff’s Office.
   B.   In addition to the conditions set forth above, the Township may
condition the issuance of a permit by imposing reasonable requirements
concerning the time, place, manner and duration of the audio and/or film
production activities as referenced on any terms and conditions that may be
attached to the permit, including but not limited to, the following:
      1.   Requirements for the presence of employees and equipment of the
Township at applicant’s expense when required for the particular audio and/or
film production activity;
      2.   Requirements concerning posting of no parking signs, placement of
traffic control devices, and employment of traffic and crowd control monitors
at applicant’s expense;
      3.   Requirements concerning the posting of the outer boundaries of the
audio and/or film production activities, and providing advance notice and
reasonable compensation to affected property owners and businesses;
      4.   Requirements concerning the cleanup and restoration of public
streets and Township property employed in the audio and/or film production
activities;
      5.   Restrictions concerning the use of Township employee services,
vehicles, and other equipment in the audio and/or film production activities;
      6.   Requirements that applicant pay all fees, deposits and obtain all
permits and licenses required for the audio and/or film production activities
under local, State and Federal law;
      7.   Restrictions on the use of firearms, explosions, and other noise-
creating or hazardous devices which disturb the peace;
      8.   Restrictions on the use of stunts involving pyrotechnics, open
flame, vehicle crashes, or other hazardous materials;
      9.   Requirements concerning cover-up of police, fire and other official
uniforms worn by actors, when the actors are not on camera;
      10.   Restrictions concerning the use of Township logos, insignias,
badges, or decals for filming purposes;
      11.   Restrictions on the daily hours the audio and/or film production
activities may be conducted in unincorporated areas of Leyden Township;
      12.   Requirements concerning the Township’s receipt of proper
acknowledgment for any assistance provided in making feature, television, or
commercial productions; and
      13.   Requirements concerning nondiscriminatory practices for employment;
and
      14.   Requirements for security and first aid. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019;
amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-10: FEES/CHARGES:
   A.   Permit Fee: Applicant shall pay a non-refundable permit fee of two
hundred dollars ($200.00) with the submittal of an application for an audio
production permit and/or film production permit.
   B.   Charges For Use Of Township Property And Personnel:
      1.   Township Property: The cost to use any building or site other than a
Township right-of-way for any use shall be one thousand seven hundred fifty
dollars ($1,750.00) per day.
      2.   Township Personnel: The cost of Township labor shall equal one and
one-half (11/2) times the hourly rate of pay for each Township employee
assigned at a two (2) hour minimum, including any overtime plus an
administrative charge equal to ten percent (10%) of total labor costs.
      3.   Public Streets Or Rights-Of-Way: For partial closure or obstruction
of any public street or right-of-way, including parking and the use of
sidewalks, the cost shall be three hundred seventy five dollars ($375.00) per
street block per day.
      4.   Equipment: The cost of Township equipment shall be calculated at the
current FEMA reimbursement rate plus an administrative charge of ten percent
(10%). Time used shall be equal to that of the operator of the equipment.
      5.   Submitting Payment: Applicant shall submit payment for all
anticipated costs of Township personnel and equipment prior to the issuance of
a permit.
   C.   Cost Of Repair And Restoration: Applicant agrees to pay in full the
cost of repair of any and all damage to public property resulting from or in
connection with the audio and/or film production activities and to restore any
area used to the same condition it was in prior to use by applicant.
   D.   Cancellation Penalties: Permittee shall pay cancellation fees as set
forth below, unless permittee gives reasonable written notice to the Township
Supervisor in advance of the proposed date of the commencement of the audio
and/or film production activities that the date of commencement needs to be
changed. In such case, the Township Supervisor is authorized to change the date
for which the audio production permit and/or film production permit has been
issued without requiring a new application or permit. The following penalties
shall otherwise be imposed for cancellation:
      1.   Four (4) business days’ or more notice - no penalty.
      2.   Three (3) business days’ notice - fifty percent (50%) of the agreed
upon cost of personnel.
      3.   Two (2) business days’ notice - seventy five percent (75%) of the
agreed upon cost of personnel.
      4.   Less than two (2) business days’ notice - one hundred percent (100%)
of the agreed upon cost of personnel.
      5.   One hundred percent (100%) of cost for any production materials
created or other Township resources used regardless of advanced notice.
   E.   Forms Of Payment: Payment may be by cashier’s check, corporate check,
money order or cash. Credit card or personal checks are not acceptable. (Ord.
TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-11: DUTIES OF PERMITTEE:
   Permittee, and all its agents, employees and contractors at the audio and/or
film production site(s) within unincorporated Leyden Township, shall comply
with the following requirements:
   A.   Permittee shall comply in writing with all terms and conditions of the
audio production permit and/or film production permit.
   B.   Permittee shall not conduct an audio or film production activity within
the unincorporated areas of Leyden Township not authorized by the audio
production permit and/or film production permit.
   C.   Permittee shall comply with instructions of the Township regarding
audio and/or film production activities.
   D.   Permittee shall comply with instructions made by Township employees
assigned to regulate the audio and/or film production activities site(s).
   E.   Permittee shall clean and restore Township-owned, leased or controlled
property utilized during the audio and/or film production activity to the same
condition as existed prior to the film production activities.
   F.   Permittee shall comply with this chapter and all other policies and
ordinances of the Township and State, County and Federal law. (Ord. TO-2019-2,
1-8-2019)
2-3-12: PYROTECHNICS:
   In addition to the audio production permit and/or film production permit,
applicant must obtain a fire permit if the audio and/or film production
activities include any special effect or stunt requiring the use of
pyrotechnics or any material deemed hazardous, including but not limited to,
fireworks, open flames, or explosives. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019)
2-3-13: PERMIT REVOCATION/SUSPENSION:
   A.   Permit Revocation: The Township may revoke the audio production permit
and/or film production permit if the permittee, or any of its agents,
employees, or contractors fail to comply with the requirements set forth in
this chapter, or if the Township determines after the permit is issued that the
permit application was false in any material detail.
      1.   Notice of the grounds for revocation of the audio production permit
and/or film production permit shall be provided in writing by the Township to
permittee or person in charge at the location of the audio and/or film
production activity.
      2.   Appeal of the permit revocation shall be conducted in the manner
provided in section
2-3-14 of this chapter.
      3.   There shall be no refundable amount due permittee under this
subsection A.
   B.   Permit Suspension: The Township may suspend the audio production permit
and/or film production permit in the event the Township Supervisor determines
either that any of the terms and conditions upon which the audio production
permit and/or film production permit was issued have been violated or that the
audio and/or film production activities pose an immediate hazard to persons or
property and permittee will not, or cannot, prevent the hazard after being
instructed to do so.
      1.   The grounds for suspension of the permit shall be provided in
writing by the Township to permittee within one business day of the suspension.
      2.   Appeal of the permit suspension shall be conducted in the manner
provided in section
2-3-14 of this chapter. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-
2023)
2-3-14: APPEALS:
   The permit applicant or permittee may appeal the denial of the audio and/or
film production permit application, revocation, suspension, permit condition,
insurance/fees requirements or the Township’s decision not to waive a deadline
set forth in this chapter to the Board of Trustees by filing an appeal in
writing with the Township Supervisor within five (5) business days after the
date the written notice of the decision is made. Failure to file a timely
appeal shall result in a waiver of the right to appeal. Appeals to the Board of
Trustees will be considered at the next regularly scheduled meeting of the
Board of Trustees following written notice of appeal.
   The Board of Trustees shall review all reliable and relevant evidence,
documents, or information and may receive and consider new evidence attached to
the written notice of appeal. After due consideration of the facts contained in
the record submitted to the Board of Trustees by the Township Supervisor, and
all other submitted materials, the Board of Trustees may: a) affirm the denial
in total; or b) overturn the denial, subject to any conditions and upon such
terms as the Board of Trustees deem necessary or appropriate to protect and
promote the public health, safety and welfare.
   The decision of the Board of Trustees shall be final. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-
2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-15: PERMIT DURATION AND EXTENSIONS:
   A.   Duration Of Permit: Any audio and/or film production permit issued
under this chapter shall be valid only for the time period specified within the
permit.
   B.   Permit Extensions: The Township Supervisor, in the exercise of the Town
Supervisor’s discretion, may approve a request for an extension of time beyond
the time specified in the permit only if all of the following conditions are
met:
      1.   Applicant shall pay an additional non-refundable one hundred dollars
($100.00) prior to the processing of the permit extension request;
      2.   The extension does not violate any of the terms and conditions of
the permit initially approved by the Township Supervisor;
      3.   Applicant shall have filed with the Township Supervisor a letter of
understanding, approved by the Township Supervisor and signed by a majority of
the owners of record and occupants of property situated within eight hundred
(800) linear feet, in each direction and on both sides of the street(s), of the
audio and/or film production and staging location(s);
      4.   Applicant shall pay any and all applicable additional fees and
charges set forth in section
2-3-10 of this chapter;
      5.   The Township Supervisor shall have determined that the requested
extension will not place an undue burden on the normal operations of the
Township; and
      6.   The Township Supervisor shall have determined that the requested
extension will not unreasonably interfere with the normal operations of schools
or businesses located with the unincorporated areas of the Township.
   C.   Extension Of Permit Conditions: In the event an extension of time
period for the audio and/or film production permit, the permit shall remain
subject to all conditions of the original permit. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019;
amd. Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022; Ord. TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-16: HOURS OF PRODUCTION:
   Audio and/or film production activities, including time for set-up, staging
and restoration, shall be limited to the following hours: Monday through
Friday, seven o’clock (7:00) A.M. to seven o’clock (7:00) P.M., and Saturday,
Sunday and holidays, eight o’clock (8:00) A.M. to six o’clock (6:00) P.M. Audio
and/or film production crews and equipment shall not arrive or stand at the
production or staging site(s) except during said hours of production. A request
for hours of production or staging beyond those specified in this section may
be approved by the Township Supervisor only after permittee has presented a
letter of understanding, approved by the Township Supervisor and signed by a
majority of the owners of record and occupants of property situated within
eight hundred (800) linear feet, in each direction and on both sides of the
street(s), of the location(s) upon which audio recording and/or filming or
staging is expected to occur. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord. TO-2023-1,
2-14-2023)
2-3-17: VEHICLE AND EQUIPMENT PARKING:
   Unless otherwise directed by the Township Supervisor and with the approval
of the Township Supervisor, vehicles, trailers and equipment shall only be
parked on one side of any Township street. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019; amd. Ord.
TO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
2-3-18: VIOLATIONS AND PENALTIES:
   A.   General Penalty: Any person who violates a provision of this chapter,
who makes a false statement in obtaining a permit under this chapter, or who
violates a condition of any permit issued under this chapter, shall be subject
to the monetary penalties imposed under section
1-4-1 of this Code. This penalty shall be in addition to any claim by the
Township under subsection
2-3-6D5 of this chapter.
   B.   Separate Offenses: Each act of violation and each day on which a
violation of this chapter or permit issued pursuant to this chapter occurs
shall constitute a separate offense.
   C.   Liability Of Permittee: Every permittee shall be subject to penalties
for violations of this chapter and for violations of the terms or conditions of
any permit issued pursuant to this chapter by any officer, director, manager,
employee, agent or representative of the permittee as if such violation had
been committed by the permittee personally. (Ord. TO-2019-2, 1-8-2019)

   The unincorporated area of Leyden Township is hereby declared a special
police district for tax purposes, in accordance with the statute in such case
made and provided. 1  (Res., 10-21-69; amd. Ord. TO-2022-1)

CHAPTER 2
PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE
SECTION:
3-2-1: Purpose; Scope; Prohibition Generally
3-2-2: Rules of Construction
3-2-3: Definitions
3-2-4: Responsibility; Maintenance Required
3-2-5: Enforcement; Penalty

3-2-7: Tree Removal
