3-2-9: House Numbering
3-2-10: Sanitation
3-2-11: Rodent Harborage
3-2-12: Grading and Drainage
3-2-13: Sidewalks and Driveways
3-2-14: Accessory Structures
3-2-15: Defacement of Property; Graffiti
3-2-16: Protective Treatment
3-2-17: Exterior Walls
3-2-18: Motor Vehicle Parking
3-2-1: PURPOSE; SCOPE; PROHIBITION GENERALLY:
   A.   Purpose: The purpose of this Property Maintenance Code is to protect,
within the unincorporated area of Leyden Township, the public health, safety
and welfare and to prevent and control blight by establishing regulations and
enforcement procedures to the end that real estate within the Township is
maintained in a safe and sanitary condition, free of health, fire and safety
hazards.
   B.   Scope: The provisions of this Property Maintenance Code shall govern
the minimum conditions and the responsibilities of persons for maintenance of
structures, equipment and exterior property.
   C.   Prohibition Generally: It shall be unlawful to commit or do any act
which endangers the public health or results in annoyance or discomfort to the
public. It shall be unlawful for any person to permit or maintain the existence
of any nuisance on any property under his/her control. Any person who shall be
responsible for the maintenance of a public nuisance, as defined in Sec.
3-2-3, below, shall be guilty of an offense. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-2: RULES OF CONSTRUCTION:
For the purposes of this Property Maintenance Code, certain terms and words are
hereby defined. Words used in the present tense shall include the future, the
singular numbers shall include the plural and the plural the singular; the word
“building” shall include the word “structure”; and the word “shall” is
mandatory and not directory. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-3: DEFINITIONS:
As used herein, the following words and terms shall have the meanings ascribed
to them in this Property Maintenance Code.
ACCESSORY      A structure the use of which is incidental to that part of the principal building
BUILDING:      and which is located on the same lot.
CODE           The person designated by the Town Supervisor and Board of Trustees of Leyden
ENFORCEMENT    Township as the code enforcement officer empowered to enforce the provisions of
OFFICER:       this Property Maintenance Code.
               The control and elimination of insects, rodents, and other pests by eliminating
EXTERMINATION: their harborage places; by removing or making inaccessible materials that may
               serve as their food; by poisoning, spraying, fumigating or trapping; or by any
               other recognized legal pest elimination methods.
               Any rejected or waste household food, offal, swill, or carrion, and every
               accumulation of animal, fruit or vegetable matter that attends the preparation,
               use, cooking and dealing in or storage of, meats, fish, fowl, fruits or
GARBAGE:       vegetables, and any other matter of any nature which are subject to decay,
               putrefaction and the generation of noxious or offensive gases or odor, or which
               during or after decay may serve as breeding or deeding material for flies or other
               germ-carrying insects.
               Any permanent display of any letter, numeral, figure, emblem, insignia, picture,
               outline, character, spectacle, delineation, announcement or any combination
               thereof which is/are painted or otherwise applied of a color different from the
GRAFFITI:      color of the exterior of the structure on which it is painted or otherwise applied
               and which size is/are visible beyond the property line boundaries of the property
               on which it is painted or otherwise applied and placed thereon without the
               permission of the owner.
INFESTATION:   The presence within or around a dwelling or dwelling unit of any insects, rodents,
               or other pests.
               Any motor vehicle which, for a period of at least seven (7) days or any longer
               period of time fixed by ordinance, the engine, wheels or other parts have been
INOPERABLE     removed, or on which the engine, wheels or other parts have been altered, damaged
MOTOR VEHICLE: or otherwise so treated that the vehicle is incapable of being driven under its
               own motor power. An inoperable motor vehicle shall not include a motor vehicle
               which has been rendered temporarily incapable of being driven under its own motor
               power in order to perform ordinary service or repair operations.
               Any discarded, used or consumed substance or waste. Litter includes, but is not
               limited to, any garbage, trash, refuse, debris, rubbish, grass clippings, or other
               lawn or garden waste, newspaper, magazine, glass, metal, plastic, or paper
LITTER:        containers, wood, motor vehicle parts, furniture, oil, carcass of dead animal,
               animal or human excrete, any nauseous or offensive material or liquid of any kind,
               any object which creates a public health or safety hazard, public nuisance or fire
               hazard or anything else of unsightly or unsanitary nature which has been
               discarded, abandoned or otherwise disposed of improperly.
OCCUPANT:      Any person living in, sleeping in or having actual possession of a building or
               portion thereof.
OPERATOR:      Any person having charge, care, management or control of any building or part
               thereof.
               Any person who, alone or jointly or severally with others, shall have legal or
               equitable title to any building, the agent of said person, or any person having
OWNER:         management or control of the building or a portion thereof, including, but not
               limited to, a purchaser, mortgagee, receiver, or lessee in possession of any
               building or portion thereof.
               Any natural person, partnership, trust, corporation or association. Whenever used
PERSON:        with respect to any penalty, the term “person” as applied to partnerships or
               associations shall mean the partners or members thereof, and as applied to trusts
               or corporations, shall mean the trustees or officers thereof.
PREMISES:      A lot, plot or parcel of land, including the buildings and structures thereon.
               For purposes of this Property Maintenance Code, “public nuisance” is any activity,
               inactivity, neglect, omission, commission, abandonment, inadvertent or otherwise,
               or the like, which does, or tends to, permits, or results in a condition or
               conditions or circumstances which deleteriously affects the public health, public
PUBLIC         safety, public welfare, public morals, public sensibilities, public rights and
NUISANCE:      enjoyment of residence or property, panders to vicious tastes, creates attractive
               nuisance for minors, results in a dilapidated, abandoned and dangerous buildings
               or improvements or unfinished or uncompleted improvements on real property,
               permits the growth of noxious or poisonous weeds or growth and accumulation of
               trash dumps or the like.
               Combustible and noncombustible waste materials, except garbage; and the term shall
               include the residue from the burning of wood, coal, coke, and other combustible
RUBBISH:       material, paper, rags, cartons, boxes, wood excelsior, rubber, leather, tree
               branches, yard trimming, tin cans, metals, mineral matter, glass crockery, dust,
               or any object that is removed from items that are presently worthless or
               unsuitable for immediate purposes.
               For the purposes of this Property Maintenance Code, “weeds” shall include, but are
               not limited to, dandelions, burdock, ragweed (giant), ragweed (common), thistle,
WEEDS:         cocklebur, jimson, blue vervain, common milk weed, wild carrot, poison ivy, mild
               mustard, rough pigweed, lambsquarter, wild lettuce, curly dock, smart weeds (all
               varieties), poison hemlock, wild hemp, and grass; except, however, weeds do not
               include cultivated flowers and gardens. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
 
3-2-4: RESPONSIBILITY; MAINTENANCE REQUIRED:
   A.   Responsibility: The owner of the premises shall maintain the structures
and exterior property in compliance with the requirements set forth in this
Property Maintenance Code, except as otherwise provided in this Town Code. A
person shall not occupy as owner-occupant or permit another person to occupy
premises that are not in a sanitary and safe condition and that do not comply
with the requirements of this Property Maintenance Code. Occupants of a
dwelling unit, rooming unit or housing unit are responsible for keeping it in a
clean, sanitary and safe condition those parts of the dwelling unit, rooming
unit, housekeeping unit or premises they occupy and control.
   B.   Vacant Structures and Land: Vacant structures and premises thereof or
vacant land shall be maintained in a clean, safe, secure and sanitary condition
as provided in this Property Maintenance Code so as to not cause a blighting
problem or adversely affect the public health or safety.
   C.   Maintenance Required: It shall be unlawful for the owner and/or
occupant of any building to fail, refuse or neglect to maintain the real estate
or building in accordance with the provisions of this Property Maintenance
Code. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-5: ENFORCEMENT; PENALTY:
   A.    Enforcement: The Township, by its duly authorized code enforcement
officer, shall have the power to enforce the provisions of this Property
Maintenance Code. If any violation is discovered by the code enforcement
officer, a citation shall be issued to the party responsible for the abatement
of the violation, setting forth the provision or the provisions of this
Property Maintenance Code deemed to be violated.
   B.   Penalty: A violation shall be subject to a fine of not less than one
hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each
offense. Every day that a violation continues shall constitute a separate
offense. The fine for the first violation shall be one hundred dollars
($100.00). The fine for the second violation shall be three hundred dollars
($300.00). The fine for the third or greater number of violations shall be five
hundred dollars ($500.00). Any citation issued for the same violation within
three (3) months of the issuance or disposition of a prior violation shall be
deemed to be the second, third, or greater number of consecutive violations as
to the same condition for the purpose of determining the amount of the fine.
Any fine paid to the Township within ten (10) days of the issuance of the
citation shall be reduced by one-half (½) of the amount of the fine set forth
on the citation. The imposition of a fine and/or the payment thereof, does not
preclude the Township from commencing proceedings for the demolition, repair or
enclosure of buildings as provided in Section 85-50 of the Illinois Township
Code (60 ILCS 1/85-50). (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-6: WEED CUTTING:
   A.   Prohibited Acts:
      1.   It shall be unlawful for the owner of any real estate in residential
areas of the Township to suffer or permit any weeds, as defined in Section
3-2-3 of this Property Maintenance Code, and grass to grow to a height of six
inches (6") or more, to remain on such property.
      2.   Every owner and/or occupant shall be required to cut the grass,
weeds or similar vegetation in the parkway immediately adjacent the front or
side yard of said real property, as necessary, so that the grass or weeds or
similar vegetation on such parkway does not exceed six inches (6") in height.
   B.   Nuisance Declared: Any weeds or grass growing to a height of six inches
(6") or greater found growing on any real estate in residential areas of the
Township are hereby declared to be a nuisance.
   C.   Removal Notice: It shall be the duty of the Town Clerk, at the
direction of the Town Supervisor or designee, to serve or cause to the owner of
real estate, on which weeds are growing in violation of this section, to be
served with a notice by United States mail, postage prepaid, directed to the
owner at the owner’s last known address demanding the removal of the weeds and
abatement of the nuisance within seven (7) days. The owner may be served by
sending notice to the person who last paid the taxes on the real estate.
   D.   Abatement of Nuisance: If the owner of real estate on which weeds are
growing refuses or neglects to cut said weeds within seven (7) days of service
of the removal notice, the Town Supervisor or his/her designee, may provide for
the cutting and removal of the weeds by Township personnel or by independent
contractors.
   E.   Removal Costs:
      1.   Weed cutting and removal work by Township personnel shall be charged
at a minimum cost of two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) for the first hour of
weed cutting and removal for the cost of mobilization, labor equipment and
overhead, and at an hourly cost of one hundred seventy-five dollars ($175.00)
for each additional hour or part thereof of weed cutting and removal work.
      2.   Weed cutting and removal work performed by independent contractors
shall be charged at the billed cost to the Township, plus fifty dollars
($50.00) for Township processing and overhead.
   F.   Bills for Services; Delinquencies:
      1.   Payment of Charges: Charges for weed cutting and removal pursuant to
subsection 3-2-6E. above, and penalty charges as provided in subsection
3-2-5B. herein, shall be included and billed as part of the Township’s periodic
bill for sewer and water utility service to the subject property, and shall be
paid at the Town Hall within fifteen days (15) after the billing date. The
property owner, and any nonowner that is the occupant or the or lessee thereof,
shall be jointly and severally liable to pay for the removal services to the
premises.
      2.   Disconnection of Utility Service for Failure to Pay Bill: If the
property owner, occupant or lessee has not paid the charges for removal as set
forth in subsection 3-2-6 E. above, and penalty charges, if any, as provided in
subsection
3-2-5B. of this Property Maintenance Code, within thirty (30) days of the date
of the issuance of the bill for such costs, utility service to the subject
property may be disconnected by the Town Supervisor or his/her designee in
accordance with the provisions set forth in section
5-1-11 of the Town Code.
   G.   Charges a Debt; Lien for Charges: The charges for unpaid weed cutting
or removal, or penalty charges billed in accordance with subsection
3-2-5B. of this Property Maintenance Code, by the Township to the owner,
occupant or lessee of the subject property, shall be a debt to the Township. If
the charges are not paid within thirty (30) days after they are due, they shall
be deemed delinquent and shall be a lien upon the real estate as provided in
section
5-4-4 of the Town Code, when such lien is filed within sixty (60) days after
the cost and expense is incurred. A change in ownership or occupancy of the
premises found delinquent shall not be a cause for reducing or eliminating
these charges or any penalties; except, however, the lien shall not be valid as
to any purchaser whose rights in and to the real estate have arisen after the
weed cutting and before the filing of the notice of lien. Additionally, said
lien shall not be valid as to any mortgagee, judgment creditor, or other
lienholder whose rights in and to the real estate arise before the filing of
said notice. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022; amd. Ord. TO 2022-13, 9-13-2022)
3-2-7: TREE REMOVAL:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful for any person to remove a tree
located on the person’s property without a written tree permit issued by the
Township. There shall be no charge for such permit. The application for the
permit shall contain the following information:
      1.   Name and address of applicant. The applicant shall be the owner of
the property or lot where the tree(s) is located;
      2.   Commonly known address of lot or property where the tree(s) sought
to be removed is located;
      3.   A written statement indicating the reason for removal of the tree
(s);
      4.   A general description of the tree(s) to be removed, including
species and size; and
      5.   Name and address of contractor or other person responsible for the
tree removal.
   B.   Duty to Remove Debris and Stumps: If the property owner hires a private
contractor to remove trees from the owner’s property, it shall be the
responsibility of the private contractor to clean up the area where the
contractor is working or has completed work and remove all branches, debris,
and largest portions of the tree(s) and dispose of such debris in such a manner
so that it will not remain on Township streets, not flow into the sewer, or
will not have to be hauled away by the Township, or its designated agent. All
stumps on Township rights-of-way and privately owned property shall be stumped
ground to depth of at least eight inches (8") below grade and all holes
remaining after stump removal shall be filled with dirt and sodded or seeded by
the property owner.
   C.   Nuisance Declared: Any bushes, branches, debris and largest portions of
the tree(s) not removed as provided in subsection 3-2-7B., above, are declared
to be a nuisance.
   D.   Removal Notice: It shall be the duty of the Town Clerk, at the
direction of the Town Supervisor or designee, to serve or cause the property
owner, on whose property the bushes, branches, debris and largest portion of
the tree(s) remain in violation of this section, to be served with a notice by
United States mail, postage prepaid, directed to the property owner at the
owner’s last known address, demanding removal of the bushes, branches, debris
and largest portion of the tree(s) within fourteen (14) days as provided in
subsection 3-2-7B., above. The property owner may be served by sending notice
to the person who last paid the taxes on the property.
   E.   Abatement of Nuisance: If the property owner refuses or neglects to
remove the bushes, branches, debris and largest portion of the tree(s), as
provided in subsection 3-2-7B., above, within fourteen (14) days of service of
the removal notice, the Town Supervisor or designee may provide for the removal
of such bushes, branches, debris and largest portion of the tree(s) by Township
personnel or by independent contractors.
   F.   Removal Costs:
      1.   Removal of the bushes, branches, debris and largest portion of the
tree(s) by Township personnel shall be charged at a minimum cost of two hundred
fifty dollars ($250.00) for the first hour of removal for the cost of
mobilization, labor equipment and overhead, and at an hourly rate of one
hundred seventy-five dollars ($175.00) for each additional hour or part thereof
for the removal of the bushes, branches, debris and largest portion of the tree
(s).
      2.   Removal of the bushes, branches, debris and largest portion of the
tree(s) performed by independent contractors shall be charged at the billed
cost, plus fifty dollars ($50.00) for Township processing and overhead.
      3.   There will be no charge for removal of the bushes, branches, debris
and largest portion of the tree(s) if the bushes, branches, debris, and largest
portion of the tree(s) to be removed was caused by an “Act of Nature”,
including, but not limited to, tornadoes, torrential rain storms, and snow
storms.
   G.   Bills for Services; Delinquencies:
      1.    Payment of Charges: Charges for removal of bushes, branches, debris
and largest portion of the tree(s) pursuant to subsection 3-2-7F., above, and
penalty charges as provided in section
3-2-5B. of the Property Maintenance Code, shall be included and billed as part
of the Township’s periodic bill for sewer and water utility service to the
subject property, and shall be paid at the Town Hall within fifteen days (15)
after the billing date. The property owner, and any nonowner that is the
occupant or the or lessee thereof, shall be jointly and severally liable to pay
for the removal services to the premises.
      2.   Disconnection of Utility Service for Failure to Pay Bill: If the
property owner, occupant or lessee has not paid the charges for removal as set
forth in subsection 3-2-7 F. above, and penalty charges, if any, as provided in
subsection
3-2-5B. of this Property Maintenance Code, within thirty (30) days of the date
of the issuance of the bill for such costs, utility service to the subject
property may be disconnected by the Town Supervisor or his/her designee in
accordance with the provisions set forth in section
5-1-11 of the Town Code.
   H.   Charges a Debt; Lien for Charges: The charges for removal of bushes,
branches, debris and largest portion of the tree(s), or penalty charges billed
in accordance with subsection
3-2-5B. of this Property Maintenance Code, by the Township to the owner,
occupant or lessee of the subject property, shall be a debt to the Township. If
the charges are not paid within thirty (30) days after they are due, they shall
be deemed delinquent and shall be a lien upon the real estate as provided in
section
5-4-4 of the Town Code, when such lien is filed within sixty (60) days after
the cost and expense is incurred. A change in ownership or occupancy of the
premises found delinquent shall not be a cause for reducing or eliminating
these charges or any penalties; except, however, the lien shall not be valid as
to any purchaser whose rights in and to the real estate have arisen after the
weed cutting and before the filing of the notice of lien. Additionally, said
lien shall not be valid as to any mortgagee, judgment creditor, or other
lienholder whose rights in and to the real estate arise before the filing of
said notice. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022; amd. Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022)
3-2-8: ABANDONED, INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
   A.   Prohibited Acts: Except as otherwise provided in the Town Code, no
person shall park, store, leave or permit the parking, storing or leaving of
any motor vehicle, trailer, or other method of conveyance of any kind which is
abandoned, wrecked, dismantled, inoperative, junked, partially dismantled, or
otherwise in a condition that constitutes a hazard to public health or safety,
whether attended or not, upon any private property within the Township for a
period of time in excess of twenty-four (24) hours. Any operable and/or
licensed motor vehicles shall be parked only on areas of hard surface pavement
and/or gravel driveways legally installed.
   B.   Unlicensed Motor Vehicles: The failure of any motor vehicle to display
an annual registration sticker or plate or a current temporary permit pending
registration or the display by a motor vehicle of an annual registration
sticker which has been expired for more than fifteen (15) days shall cause the
motor vehicle to be considered inoperative for the purpose of this section.
   C.   Exception: This section does not apply to any motor vehicle entirely
enclosed within a building on private property when not in use; any motor
vehicle held in connection with a business enterprise (i.e., place of business
engaged in the wrecking or junking of motor vehicles), lawfully licensed and
properly operated in the appropriate zoning district, pursuant to the zoning
laws of Cook County; or to operable historic vehicles over twenty-five (25)
years of age.
   D.   Nuisance Declared: Any motor vehicle in violation of subsection 3-2-
8A., above, is hereby declared to be a nuisance.
   E.   Enforcement and Penalties:
      1   Notice to Remove:
         a.   Public Ways: Wherever the Town Board or its named designate, or
the Highway Commissioner of the Town or the Highway Commissioner’s named
designate sends notice to the last owner of such vehicle, as registered with
the Secretary of State, to dispose of such inoperable motor vehicle, it shall
be unlawful for such owner to permit the said vehicle, or parts thereof, to
remain upon the public way after the passage of seven (7) days from the
forwarding of such notice by mail or personal delivery.
         b.   Private Ways: Wherever the Town Board or its named designate, or
the Highway Commissioner of the Town or the Highway Commissioner’s named
designate sends notice to the last owner of such vehicle, as registered with
the Secretary of State, to dispose of such inoperable motor vehicle, it shall
be unlawful for such owner to permit the said vehicle, or parts thereof, to
remain upon the private way after the passage of seven (7) days from the
forwarding of such notice by mail or personal service upon the registered owner
or some occupant of the owner’s household over the age of ten (10) years.
      2.   Removal by Enforcing Authorities; Costs: The State’s Attorney’s
office or the police department of any municipality located totally or
partially within the Township are hereby authorized to remove or cause to be
removed such inoperable motor vehicle or parts thereof.
The reasonable cost of such removal shall be charged and paid by such
registered owner upon billing thereof.
      3.   Penalties:
         a.   A fine of twenty five dollars ($25.00) per day for each day that
the registered owner fails to obey the notice of the Township and permits such
vehicle, or parts thereof, to remain upon the public way seven (7) days after
such notice herein made and provided for is hereby imposed upon such registered
owner. Each day after the expunction of the said seven (7) days, as aforesaid,
shall be considered a separate offense.
         b.   A fine of twenty five dollars ($25.00) per day for each day that
the registered owner fails to obey the notice of the Township and permits such
vehicle, or parts thereof, to remain upon the private way seven (7) days after
such notice herein made and provided for is here imposed upon such registered
owner. Each day after the expunction of the said seven (7) days, as aforesaid,
shall be considered a separate offense. (Ord., eff. 1-1-88; amd. Ord. TO-2022-
1, 2-8-2022; Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022)
3-2-9: HOUSE NUMBERING:
   A.   Compliance: It is hereby made the duty of the owner, agent or person in
possession of any buildings in unincorporated Leyden Township to number the
building in the manner provided by this section.
   B.   Placement of Numbers; Size of Numbers:
      1.   Each building to which a house number has been assigned shall have
the house number displayed upon the building.
      2.   The assigned house number shall be either affixed directly to the
building or posted or displayed upon a sign affixed to the building or posted
in a prominent position. The house number shall be displayed in such a manner
so that the numbers contrast in color with the background and shall be
observable and readable by those traveling in either direction on the adjoining
public street or other thoroughfare providing access to the building. If the
building has an unattached mailbox, the assigned house number shall be affixed
on both sides of said mailbox.
      3.   All numbers shall be in standard Arabic Numbers. Not less than three
(3) inches in height and shall be reflective for visibility during nighttime
hours.
      4.   If the house number posted on the building is not readily
identifiable from the roadway fronting the building, then the number shall be
affixed to the building as well as posted by the roadway. If the building has
multiple house numbers or apartment numbers (i.e., professional buildings,
multi-family residences), a building directory shall be posted at the main
entrance to the building.
      5.   The house numbers shall be placed as to not be obstructed by trees,
shrubbery or other foliage, or any extension of the building.
   C.   Removing, Defacing Numbers: No person shall willfully deface or remove
any number required by this section which has been placed upon any building.
(TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-10: SANITATION:
Exterior property and premises shall be maintained in a clean, safe and
sanitary condition, free of any accumulation of rubbish, litter or garbage. The
owner and/or occupant shall keep that part of the exterior property that such
occupant occupies or controls in a clean and sanitary condition.
   A.   Accumulation of Rubbish or Garbage. Exterior property and premises, and
the interior of every structure, shall be free from any accumulation of rubbish
or garbage.
   B.   Garbage Storage and Disposal. Every owner and/or occupant of a dwelling
unit shall store and dispose of garbage, refuse, and any other matter of any
nature which are subject to decay, putrefaction and the generation of noxious
or offensive gases or flies or other insects, rodents, or other pests in a
clean, sanitary and safe manner, so as not to become a public nuisance. Garbage
and refuse shall be properly disposed and kept in an approved container as
provided in Chapter 4, “Waste Disposal Regulations” , of Title 3, of the Town
Code.
   C.   Containers. The operator of every establishment, producing garbage and
rubbish, that is not a “Covered Unit”, as defined in Section 3-4-1 of Chapter
4, Title 3 of the Town Code, shall provide, and at all times cause to be
utilized, approved leakproof containers provided with close-fitting covers for
the storage of such materials, as provided in Chapter 4, Title 3, until removed
from the premises for disposal.
   D.   Refrigerators. Refrigerators and similar equipment (i.e., “White
Goods”, as defined in Section 3-4-1 of Chapter 4, Title 3), not in operation
shall not be discarded, abandoned or stored on premises without first removing
the doors. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-11: RODENT HARBORAGE:
Structures and exterior property shall be kept free from rodent harborage and
infestation. Where rodents are found, they shall be promptly exterminated by
approved processes that will not be injurious to human health. After pest
elimination, proper precautions shall be taken to eliminate rodent harborage
and prevent reinfestation. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-12: GRADING AND DRAINAGE:
Premises shall be graded and maintained to prevent the erosion of soil and to
prevent the accumulation of stagnant water thereon, or within any structure
located thereon; except, however, approved retention areas and reservoirs. (TO-
2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-13: SIDEWALKS AND DRIVEWAYS:
Sidewalks, walkways, stairs, driveways, parking spaces, and similar areas shall
be kept in a proper state of repair, and maintained free of loose or broken
material and cracks and other hazardous conditions. All means of ingress and
egress from any building shall be maintained in good repair and free from any
obstructions, including vegetation. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-14: ACCESSORY STRUCTURES:
Accessory structures, including detached garages, fences, tool sheds, walls and
other out-buildings, shall be maintained structurally sound, in good repair,
and secured through working doors so as not to be unsafe or harborage for
insects, rodents, and other pests. Fences shall be maintained in a good state
of repair free from loose or deteriorating members. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-15: DEFACEMENT OF PROPERTY; GRAFFITI:
   A.   A person shall not willfully or wantonly damage, mutilate or deface any
exterior surface of any structure or building on any private or public property
by placing thereon any marking, carving or graffiti. It shall be the
responsibility of the owner to restore said surface to an approved state of
maintenance and repair.
   B.   It shall be unlawful for the owner or occupant of any property to allow
any graffiti sign painted or otherwise applied on an exterior wall of a
building or any structure upon that property to remain thereon for more than
fourteen (14) days. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-16: PROTECTIVE TREATMENT:
Exterior surfaces, including but not limited to, doors, door and window frames,
cornices, porches, trim, balconies, decks and fences, shall be maintained in
good condition. Exterior wood surfaces, other than decay-resistant woods, shall
be protected from the elements and decay by painting or other protective
covering or treatment. Peeling, flaking and chipped paint shall be eliminated
and surfaces repainted. Siding and masonry joints, as well as those between the
building envelope and the perimeter of windows, doors and skylights, shall be
maintained weather resistant and water tight. Metal surfaces subject to rust or
corrosion shall be coated to inhibit such rust and corrosion, and surfaces with
rust or corrosion shall be stabilized and coated to inhibit future rust and
corrosion. Oxidation stains shall be removed from exterior surfaces. Surfaces
designed for stabilization by oxidation are exempt from this requirement. (TO-
2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-17: EXTERIOR WALLS:
Exterior walls shall be free from holes, breaks, and loose or rotting
materials; and maintained weatherproof and properly surface coated where
required to prevent deterioration. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-2-18: MOTOR VEHICLE PARKING:
No motor vehicle shall be parked on any lot unless parked on a concrete or
asphalt driveway. (TO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
CHAPTER 3
PUBLIC WAYS PROPERTY MAINTENANCE CODE
SECTION:
3-3-1: Purpose
3-3-2: Enforcement
3-3-3: Penalties
3-3-4: Discharge Of Sewage Into Open Ditches Along Township Streets And
Highways
3-3-5: Deposit Of Snow Or Ice upon Public Highway; Prohibition
3-3-6: Water Drainage Onto Township Property
3-3-7: Deposit Of Refuse, Garbage And Litter On Township Road District Property
3-3-8: Debris And Vegetation
3-3-9: Repairs To Motor Vehicles On Public Ways; Broken Windows
3-3-10: Abandoned, Inoperable Vehicles
3-3-11: Removal Of Animal Waste
3-3-12: Excessive Noise On Public Property
3-3-13: Restraint Of Animals
3-3-1: PURPOSE:
A serious problem deleterious to the health, welfare and safety of the citizens
of the Town of Leyden exists by reason of the actions of certain citizens in
disposing or causing to be depositing of garbage, abandoning vehicles,
discharge of sewage, depositing of snow and ice, water drainage, debris and
vegetation, junk and other waste on the public ways and property of the
Township. Such actions also hampers and prevents the Town of Leyden, its
various agencies, departments and the Highway Commissioner from their
respective statutory duties. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-2: ENFORCEMENT:
   A.   The person designated by the Town Supervisor and Board of Trustees as
the Leyden Township Code Enforcement Officer is empowered to enforce the
provisions of this Public Ways Property Maintenance Code.
   B.   Violation of this Public Ways Property Maintenance Code shall be deemed
a nuisance which may be abated by the Highway Commissioner, Town Supervisor or
Town Attorney who may enforce this Code through injunctive or other relief ,
including prosecution for a fine as set forth in Section
3-3-3 below. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-3: PENALTIES:
   A.   Any person or entity who shall violate any provision of this Public
Ways Property Maintenance Code shall be fined not less than twenty-five dollars
($25.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for each offense, plus
any attorney fees and court costs. A separate and distinct offense shall be
deemed committed on each day during which a violation occurs or continues.
   B.   Collection and Payment of Fees: Any fines collected by the Township for
offenses committed under this Public Ways Property Maintenance Code upon any
highway or right-of-way maintained by or under the supervision of the Leyden
Township Highway Commissioner shall be paid to and deposited into the Township
Road and Bridges fund. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-4: DISCHARGE OF SEWAGE INTO OPEN DITCHES ALONG TOWNSHIP STREETS AND
HIGHWAYS:
Prohibited Acts: It shall be unlawful for any person or entity, whether public
or private, to discharge or empty any type of sewage, including the effluent
from septic tanks or other sewage treatment devices, or any other domestic,
commercial or industrial waste, or any putrescible liquids, or cause the same
to be discharged or emptied in any manner into open ditches along any public
street or highway, or into any drain or drainage structure installed solely for
street or highway drainage purposes. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-5: DEPOSIT OF SNOW OR ICE UPON PUBLIC HIGHWAY; PROHIBITION:
It shall be unlawful for any person or entity to remove or cause to be plowed
or removed snow or ice from private property onto property belonging to the
Township, including but not limited to parkways, streets, sidewalks, easements,
and rights-of-way under the jurisdiction of the Highway Commissioner. (Ord. HO-
2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-6: WATER DRAINAGE ONTO TOWNSHIP PROPERTY:
It shall be unlawful for any person to cause or allow water to drain or
discharge unnaturally from private property onto Township property including,
but not limited to, parkways, streets, sidewalks, easements, and rights-of-way
under the jurisdiction of the Highway Commissioner without express written
authorization of the Highway Commissioner. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022; amd. Ord.
HO-2023-1, 2-14-2023)
3-3-7: DEPOSIT OF REFUSE, GARBAGE AND LITTER ON TOWNSHIP ROAD DISTRICT
PROPERTY:
Except as provided in Chapter 4, “Waste Disposal Regulations”, Title 3 of the
Town Code, no person or entity shall deposit refuse, garbage, litter, or any
can, container or other receptacles, whether empty or containing the same, on
rights-of-way, streets, parkways, or other property belonging to or under the
jurisdiction of the Highway Commissioner. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-8: DEBRIS AND VEGETATION:
   A.   It shall be unlawful for any person or entity to cause or allow any
debris, refuse, tree limbs, tree trunks, leaves, grass clippings and/or other
types of vegetation to be placed upon any property belonging to the Township,
including but not limited to parkways, streets, sidewalks, easements, and
rights-of-way under the jurisdiction of the Highway Commissioner. Placement of
said items on parkways, streets, sidewalks, easements and rights-of-way is
prohibited without the express approval of the Highway Commissioner.
   B.   This Section shall not apply to scheduled garbage pick-up in compliance
with Chapter 4, “Waste Disposal Regulations”, and Section
3-2-7, “Tree Removal”, of Chapter 2, Title 3 of the Town Code, or to any other
refuse collection sponsored or authorized by the Highway Commissioner and/or
the Town Supervisor. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-9: REPAIRS TO MOTOR VEHICLES ON PUBLIC WAYS; BROKEN WINDOWS:
   A.   Repairs: It shall be unlawful for anyone to change any parts, repair,
wash, grease, wax, polish or clean a motor vehicle on any public streets,
roads, alleys ,and rights-of-way under the jurisdiction of the Highway
Commissioner except such repairs, cleaning or polishing as is necessary to
ensure good vision, or such emergency repairs as are necessary to remove such
motor vehicle from the public way. Such emergency repairs shall be made only as
close as possible to the right-edge of the roadway, with the motor vehicle
facing in the direction of the traffic flow.
   B.   Broken Windows: It shall be unlawful for any motor vehicle with a
broken window to remain on any public street, road, alley and right-of-way
under the jurisdiction of the Highway Commissioner for more than twenty-four
(24) hours. After twenty-four (24) hours, the motor vehicle shall be towed at
the owner’s expense.
      1.   Any motor vehicle in violation of this Section may be towed to a
safe storage place where it shall be held until claimed by the owner. The owner
shall be required to pay towing and storage charges.
      2.   The Highway Commissioner is authorized to contract with any
municipality or private towing company, to ticket, tow or otherwise enforce
this Section. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-10: ABANDONED, INOPERABLE VEHICLES:
   A.   Inoperable Motor Vehicle Defined:
      1.   “Inoperable motor vehicle” means any motor vehicle from which, for a
period of at least seven (7) days or any longer period of time fixed by
ordinance, the engine, wheels or other parts have been removed, or on which the
engine, wheels or other parts have been altered, damaged or otherwise so
treated that the vehicle is incapable of being driven under its own motor
power.
      2.   “Inoperable motor vehicle” shall not include a motor vehicle which
has been rendered temporarily incapable of being driven under its own motor
power in order to perform ordinary service or repair operations.
   B.   Nuisance Declared: The Highway Commissioner hereby declares that
inoperable vehicles on public ways under the jurisdiction of the Highway
Commissioner to be a nuisance.
   C.   Notice to Remove: Whenever the Highway Commissioner or his/her
designated agent sends a notice to the last owner of an inoperable vehicle
located on a public way, as registered with the Secretary of State, to dispose
of such inoperable vehicle, it shall be unlawful for such owner to permit said
vehicle, or parts thereof, to remain upon the public ways after the passage of
seven (7) days from the issuance of the notice by mail or personal delivery.
   D.   Removal by Enforcing Authorities; Costs: The Cook County Sheriff’s
Office or the police department of any municipality located totally or
partially within the Township are hereby authorized to remove or cause to be
removed such inoperable motor vehicle or parts thereof. The reasonable cost of
such removal shall be charged and paid by the registered owner of the
inoperable motor vehicle upon the billing thereof.
   E.   Penalties: A fine of fifty dollars ($50.00) per day for each day that
the registered owner fails to obey the notice of the Highway Commissioner and
permits such inoperable vehicle, or parts thereof, to remain upon the public
ways seven (7) days after such notice herein is made, shall be imposed upon
such registered owner. Each day after the expiration of said seven (7) days
shall be a separate offense. (Ord. HO-2022-1, 2-8-2022)
3-3-11: REMOVAL OF ANIMAL WASTE:
   A.   No person shall permit any animal in their custody or control to enter
upon public property including, but not limited to, public parks, public roads,
and public ways, and defecate or deposit excrement, feces or waste onto such
public property, unless such person immediately and effectively removes and
disposes of such waste in a clean and sanitary manner.
   B.   Any person found to have been in violation of this section shall be
fined not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred dollars
($500.00) for each offense.
(Ord. TO-2024-7, 5-14-2024; amd. HO 2024-5, 5-14-2024)
3-3-12: EXCESSIVE NOISE ON PUBLIC PROPERTY:
   A.   No person shall make, cause, permit, or allow any excessive noise upon
Township property including, but not limited to, public parks, public roads,
and public ways, or in such close proximity to such public property as to be
distinctly and loudly audible upon such public property, that unreasonably
disturbs the peace, health, or safety of the neighborhood within the area of
audibility. Any such noise that occurs during the closing hours of Township
parks shall be prima facie evidence of a violation of this section.
   B.   Any person found to have been in violation of this section shall be
fined not less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than fivve hundred dollars
($500.00) for each offense.
(Ord. TO-2024-9, 6-11-2024; amd. Ord. HO 2024-6, 6-11-2024)
3-3-13: RESTRAINT OF ANIMALS
No person shall permit any animal in their custody or control to enter upon
public property including, but not limited to, public parks, public roads, and
public ways, without securing the animal by a leash or other restraint.
Any person found to have been in violation of this section shall be fined not
less than fifty dollars ($50.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00)
for each offense. (Ord. TO 2024-13, 9-10-2024; amd. Ord. HO-2024-8, 9-10-2024)

3-4-2: LEYDEN TOWNSHIP SPECIAL REFUSE COLLECTION AND DISPOSAL DISTRICT:
   This chapter shall be applicable only in unincorporated Leyden Township
heretofore declared a special refuse collection and disposal district. (Ord.
TO-92-1, 1-14-1992)
3-4-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
   A.   General: No person shall dispose of any waste except as permitted in
this chapter.
   B.   Disposal Of Waste On Public Property: No person shall deposit, abandon,
dump, or place any waste, or cause any waste to be deposited, abandoned, dumped
or placed on any street, sidewalk, alley or other public property, except that
the owner of any premises may place waste generated on said premises at the
curbside of the abutting public street or other approved collection area during
the period provided in subsection
3-4-4E of this chapter prior to the time the waste is scheduled to be removed
by a licensed waste hauler, provided that the waste is within containers
complying with this chapter.
   C.   Disposal Of Waste On Private Property: No person other than the owner
shall deposit, abandon, dump or dispose of any waste on any privately owned
property. The owner of the property may do so only as provided in subsections
3-4-4E and
3-4-6C of this chapter.
   D.   Open Dumping: No person shall cause or allow the open dumping of any
waste within the district.
   E.   Conducting Waste Facilities: No person shall conduct any waste
collection, removal, treatment or disposal operation in the district without a
license hereunder.
   F.   Waste Subjected To The Elements: No person shall store, cast, throw,
drop, place or deposit any waste in such a manner that the waste may be carried
by the action of the sun, wind, rain or snow into or upon any street, sidewalk,
alley, park or other public or private place in the district or into or upon
adjacent premises.
   G.   Unauthorized Waste Removal: No person other than the town, a licensed
waste hauler or a licensed junk dealer shall remove any waste from any premises
in the district. This subsection shall not apply to the removal of discarded
bulk items or white goods by vendors of such items upon purchase of
replacements.
   H.   Disturbing Waste Containers: No person other than the town, a licensed
waste hauler, or the owner of the premises shall displace, uncover or in any
way disturb a waste container or the contents of a waste container located on
any premises in the district.
   I.   Removal Of Nonmunicipal Waste: Subsections G and H of this section
shall not apply to the collection and removal of any nonmunicipal waste by
authorized waste haulers for disposal, treatment or storage at a site or
facility meeting the requirements of the Illinois environmental protection act
and the Illinois pollution control board, provided such collection and removal
is with the permission of the owner of the premises. (Ord. TO-92-1, 1-14-1992)
   J.   Accumulation Of Waste: No person shall store, dump, or permit the
accumulation of debris, refuse, garbage, trash, compost or any other waste in a
manner that may harbor mosquitoes, flies, insects, rodents, vermin or other
disease carrying animals, that creates a nuisance, results in noxious or
offensive smells, or that is otherwise offensive or dangerous to the public
health. (Ord. SWO-2001-3, 9-18-2001)
3-4-4: COLLECTION:
   A.   General: The town supervisor shall have charge of the municipal waste
collection, recycling and disposal program for the district, and the
enforcement of this chapter.
   B.   Contracting Waste Haulers: The Town may contract with one or more duly
qualified and licensed waste haulers for the collection, removal and disposal
of ashes, garbage, refuse, landscape waste, recyclable waste, electronic waste,
and household hazardous waste.
   C.   Scheduling Of Collections: The scheduling of pick-up hours, days and
routes for all waste removal for covered units shall be determined by written
agreement executed by the Town Supervisor and a licensed waste hauler.
   D.   Duties Of Customers/Covered Units: It shall be the duty of each
customer in the District to:
      1.   Utilize landscape waste containers as specified in section
3-4-6 of this chapter for disposal and pick up of landscape waste.
      2.   Utilize recycling waste containers as specified in section
3-4-6 of this chapter for disposal and pick-up of landscape waste.
      3.   Utilize refuse containers as specified in section
3-4-8 of this chapter for disposal and pick up of garbage, ashes and refuse.
      4.   Utilize the waste collection and disposal services offered by the
licensed waste hauler under contract with the town to the extent such services
are made available to persons in the district.
      5.   Promptly pay the waste collection and disposal charges billed
directly to owners of property in the district in accordance with the rates and
pursuant to the terms set forth in the town's waste removal contract with its
licensed waste hauler(s), now in effect or as hereafter approved, amended,
modified or replaced.
      6.   Comply with the provisions of this chapter as now in effect or
hereafter amended, including any rules and regulations hereafter adopted,
amended, modified or replaced.
   E.   Time And Place Of Setting Waste Out For Collection: Landscape waste
containers, recycling waste containers, and bulk items shall be placed at the
curbside of the road adjacent to the covered unit's premises on the regularly
or specially scheduled pick-up day or days for such materials. These
receptacles and items shall not be placed out for collection before five
o'clock (5:00) P.M. of the day prior to pick up and shall be removed from the
pick-up area by nine o'clock (9:00) P.M. on the day of pick-up.
   F.   Duties Of Waste Haulers: The services to be rendered by any waste
hauler operating within unincorporated Leyden Township shall be performed with
due care and in a professional, orderly, efficient and workmanlike manner. In
addition:
      1.   Any waste hauler operating within the District must have and
maintain all necessary federal, state and local permits, licenses and
qualifications for municipal solid waste collection and disposal as may be
necessary to lawfully perform such services.
      2.   Waste haulers must employ a workforce adequate in number, training
and equipment to accomplish the same on a regular basis despite adverse
conditions, breakdowns or similar hindrances. Waste haulers shall not litter
streets or any customer's premises in the process of making collections nor
allow any municipal waste to blow, fall or spill from any vehicle used for
collections. Waste haulers shall repair or replace, at its expense, containers
damaged as a result of its handling thereof, reasonable wear and tear excepted.
Waste haulers shall replace lids or covers on containers immediately after
emptying. Waste haulers' employees shall close all fence gates both upon
entering and leaving premises and shall not cut across rear, front, or side
yards, or flower beds to adjoining premises without permission of the owner.
      3.   Waste haulers shall use only fully enclosed, modern, packer-type
trucks in good working order and in a clean and sanitary condition in
collecting garbage, ashes and refuse (excluding bulk items and White Goods).
      4.   Waste haulers shall use enclosed vehicles and/or covers to prevent
any loss, spillage or blowing of materials during the transfer or
transportation of municipal waste to a disposal facility.
      5.   Waste haulers shall immediately clean up and collect any municipal
waste spilled or lost during collection or transportation, without regard to
whether the waste hauler caused the material to be spilled or lost.
      6.   All services by a waste hauler, either under contract with or
licensed by the Town, shall be performed by the waste hauler's employees in a
neat, orderly and courteous manner, without causing loud or raucous noises,
bright lights or other nuisance and with due care and regard for the safety,
peace and quietude of all other persons while engaged in waste collection and
disposal.
      7.   No waste hauler or its employees shall consume or be under the
influence of any alcoholic beverage or controlled substances (except by
doctor's prescription and subject to such doctor's work restrictions)
immediately prior to or during the course of performing their duties under a
contract with the Town or this chapter. Waste haulers shall not suffer or
permit their employees to perform services under a contract with the Town or
this chapter while actually or apparently under the influence of alcohol or
drugs.
      8.   Waste haulers shall collect and remove all waste (with the exception
of exempt waste, absent special arrangements) set for collection by an owner/
renter of property in the District notwithstanding any dispute as to the manner
in which the waste is set out for placement or the contents of the waste,
provide that the waste is not of such a nature that the operator of the
disposal facility will have cause to reject the waste.
      9.   Waste haulers shall tag any waste set out for collection by an
owner/renter of property in the District, but which is not collectable, with a
tag explaining why such waste was not collected and the requirements, if any,
for arranging collection and disposal of the waste.
      10.   Waste haulers must carry and maintain, at its sole expense,
worker's compensation insurance, motor vehicle liability insurance and general
comprehensive liability insurance in amounts and subject to terms and
conditions as the Town may provide in its written agreement with a waste hauler
or as a condition to issuance of a license to collect and dispose of waste in
the District.
      11.   Waste haulers shall comply with all federal, state and local
regulations on the disposal of special and hazardous waste materials.
   G.   Uncollectable Waste: All waste not subject to collection by the
licensed waste haulers under contract with the Town shall be disposed of by the
owner of the premises in which the waste is produced or located in accordance
with the provisions of this Chapter and applicable Federal, State and local
requirements. (Ord. TO-92-1, 1-14-1992; amd. Ord. TO-2021-17, 12-14-2021)
3-4-5: NONRESIDENTIAL; COMMERCIAL WASTE:
   A.   Removal Of Waste: To the extent that waste collection and disposal
services offered by the Town under contract through its licensed waste hauler
(s) are not made available to owners of property in the District, the duties
set forth in subsection
3-4-4D4, 5 and 6 shall not be applicable. In that event, such owners must
provide for the removal of waste from the premises by a licensed scavenger
service as often as necessary to prevent the creation of a nuisance, but no
less often than once a week. Otherwise, all provisions of this Chapter shall be
applicable.
   B.   Containers: All waste generated for disposal on property in the
District shall be deposited in containers which meet the requirements of
Sections
3-4-6,
3-4-7 and
3-4-8 of this Chapter.
   C.   Pick-Up: Nonresidential waste/commercial waste pick-ups shall be at the
alley to the rear of the building to be served, or in the designated "garbage
area" located on the premises, provided that such designation meets the prior
approval of the building owner and the waste hauler. (Ord. TO-92-1, 1-14-1992;
amd. Ord. TO-2021-17, 12-14-2021)
3-4-6: LANDSCAPE WASTE:
   A.   Mandatory Separation; Disposal: No person shall combine landscape waste
with any other household waste for the purposes of disposal or collection. No
person shall set landscape waste out for collection in any container other than
the landscape waste containers described in subsection E of this section.
   B.   All landscape waste haulers shall dispose all landscape waste at a
lawfully operated and duly licensed and/or permitted disposal facility, unless
otherwise directed by the Town pursuant to an agreement or license conditions
to dispose of landscape waste in a particular site or location. A facility may
treat, compost, grind, or land apply said landscape waste. No landscape waste
may be disposed of at a landfill or solid waste incinerator unless otherwise
authorized by the Illinois Environmental Agency (IEPA).
   C.   Composting: No person shall compost landscape waste in the District
without a permit therefor unless the waste was generated on the property on
which it is to be composted. The Town encourages and permits mulching and/or
composting of landscape waste on the property on which it was generated
provided that such mulching or composting is performed so as not to create a
nuisance.
   D.   Open Burning: No person shall burn any accumulations of landscape waste
on any private or public property.
   E.   Landscape Waste Containers:
      1.   Landscape waste shall be placed into bags, which shall be flat
bottom thirty (30) gallon paper bags of a minimum two (2) ply, fifty (50) pound
wet strength Kraft paper, with approximate dimensions of sixteen inches by
twelve inches by thirty five inches (16" x 12" x 35"), or other biodegradable
paper bags of comparable size and quality. Plastic bags, whether described as
"biodegradable" or not, shall not be permitted except by prior written
agreement between the waste hauler and the Town.
      2.   Landscape waste generated on the premises of customers/covered units
for collection by the licensed waste hauler under contract with the Town may
also be placed in an approved thirty-two (32) gallon container that is clearly
marked with a sixteen inch (16") red painted "X" on both sides. This container
shall not weigh more than fifty (50) pounds when full.
   F.   Landscape Brush, Branches And Shrubbery: Loose brush, branches and
shrubbery cuttings (four inches (4") or less in diameter), if securely tied in
bundles not exceeding four feet (4') in length and sixty (60) pounds in weight,
shall be collected by the waste hauler if the bundle is properly placed at the
curbside for pick-up.
   G.   Costs: The cost of curbside collection and disposal of landscape waste,
including landscape brush, branches and shrubbery as described in subsection F
above, from customers/covered units, will be charged to the customers/covered
units by the waste hauler under contract with the Town as part of the municipal
solid waste collection, removal and disposal services.
   H.   Quantity Subject To Weekly Collection: There shall be no limit as to
the number of landscape waste containers or properly bundled brush, branches
and shrubbery which may be deposited by customers/covered units for pick-up by
the waste hauler under contract with the Town.
   I.   Enclosed Storage Of Landscape Waste: No person shall store, place or
deposit any landscape waste, except firewood, within an enclosed structure. All
firewood stored within an enclosed structure must be stored in a place and
manner so that it is not susceptible to spontaneous combustion.
   J.   Blowing Or Drifting Waste: All persons shall exercise due care to
prevent accumulations of landscape waste from blowing or drifting onto the
property of another.
   K.   Prohibition On Use Of Landscape Waste Collection Service And
Containers:
      1.   No person shall mix landscape waste with other waste materials in
any landscape waste collection containers. No landscape waste containers shall
be placed for pickup if they contain nonlandscape waste materials.
      2.   No person shall place any landscape waste for collection by the
licensed waste hauler under contract with the Town if such waste was not
generated on the premises of the residential customer placing such waste for
collection at the curbside of the person’s property.
      3.   No residential customer shall suffer or permit any other person to
place landscape waste not generated on the customer’s premises in landscape
waste containers placed for collection from customer’s premises.
      4.   All landscape, lawn or yard services shall contract separately for
removal and/or disposal of landscape waste generated within or without the
District. No person may place any landscape waste collected through such
services for regular collection from the premises of residential customers by
the licensed waste hauler under contract with the Town.
      5.   No landscape, lawn or yard service may deposit landscape waste in
any centralized landscape waste drop-off container as may be provided by the
Town. (Ord. TO-92-1, 1-14-1992; amd. Ord. TO-2021-17, 12-14-2021; Ord. TO-2022-
13, 9-13-2022)
3-4-7: RECYCLABLE WASTE:
   A.   Mandatory Separation:
      1.   All recyclables shall be separated from all other waste for the
purposes of disposal and collection. The recyclables collected shall be
separated and otherwise treated so as to facilitate the sale of said materials
to processing companies or recycled material brokers.
      2.   Subject to the existence of a viable market, the Town Supervisor is
authorized to designate additional categories or eliminate existing categories
of recyclable materials for separation, collection and disposal.
      3.   All designated recyclable materials, except newsprint, shall be
rinsed and stripped of any lids, stoppers, packaging or labels before being
placed in the appropriate recycling cart for collection and disposal.
   B.   Picking Prohibited: It shall be unlawful for any waste collection
service, hauler, recycler, or other entity or person to remove, collect,
obtain, possess or pick any item of recyclable waste placed for collection as
part of the town's recycling program, except pursuant to contract and/or
license from the town. When placed for collection, designated recyclable waste
items shall be considered property of the town. When collected by the town's
licensed recyclable waste hauler, recyclable waste items shall be the property
of the town's recyclable waste hauler.
   C.   Containers: Recyclables shall only be placed in a roll-out cart
provided by the waste hauler under contract with the Town or in rigid plastic
recycling bins previously distributed by the Town. The Town or the waste hauler
shall continue to own the recycling containers distributed. Each customer shall
be responsible for the reasonable care of its recycling containers. When any
customer relocates outside the Township, the customer must return the recycling
containers to the Town.
   D.   Recycling Facilities: It is to be the duty of any recyclable waste
hauler under contract with and/or licensed by the town to have available at all
relevant times one or more recycling facilities, with all necessary or
appropriate federal, state and local permits, licenses or approvals, for the
collection, sorting and recycling of recyclable waste generated for disposal
under its contract with the town and/or this chapter. The recyclable waste
hauler shall dispose of all recyclable waste at such a facility unless
otherwise directed by the town to dispose of the recyclable waste in a
particular site or location. No recyclable waste may be disposed of at a
landfill or in any other way than by recycling without approval by the town.
   E.   Quantity Of Recyclable Waste Subject To Weekly Collection: There shall
be no limit on the quantity of recyclable waste to be collected from each
residential property during each regularly scheduled collection provided that
all recyclable waste set out for collection was generated in the normal course
of use of the premises.
   F.   Exclusive Use Of Containers For Recycling: No person shall place or
deposit anything except designated recyclable waste in any recycling cart for
pick up and collection.
   G.   Public Education: The town supervisor or the town's licensed recyclable
waste hauler shall publish and distribute information to each residential
customer in the district on the mandatory recycling program along with
educational materials explaining the recycling process and its benefits. (Ord.
TO-92-1, 1-14-1992; amd. Ord. TO-2014-5, 10-14-2014; amd. Ord. 2019-6, 5-14-
2019; Ord. TO-2021-17, 12-14-2021)
3-4-8: REFUSE:
   A.   Collection: Owners of property in the District shall provide for
collection, removal and disposal of refuse generated on their premises at least
once a week. Refuse shall be placed in containers as described in this section
and set out for collection as set forth in subsection
3-4-4E of this chapter.
      1.   Residents shall be allowed to place up to two (2) cubic yards of
household construction and demolition debris generated by "do-it-yourself"
projects as part of regular refuse set-outs. Larger quantities of household
construction and demolition debris shall require special pick-up service
pursuant to subsection G of this section.
   B.   Containers:
      1.   Customers/Covered Units (One And Two-Family Residences): All refuse
to be collected in the regular weekly customer service shall be placed in
approved containers except for such items as are too bulky to fit in said
containers. An approved container for customers shall mean a roll-out cart or a
container of standard waterproof construction and made of durable, rigid, heavy
duty plastic, aluminum, galvanized steel or other acceptable metal with a
tight-fitting cover and with handles suitable for lifting by one (1) person.
Except as hereinafter provided, such containers shall have a capacity of not
less than ten (10) gallons nor more than thirty-two (32) gallons, and not weigh
more than fifty (50) pounds when filled. Subject to the provisions of
subsection G, there shall no limit to the number of approved refuse containers
customers may place for curbside pick-up by the waste hauler under contract
with the Town.
         a.   Each Customer/Covered Unit shall be provided with one (1) Roll-
Out Cart for Refuse and one (1) Roll-Out Cart for Recyclables. If the Customer
requests additional Refuse and/or Recycling carts, the price shall be as
follows:
            (1)   One additional cart - $5.00 per month.
            (2)   Two or more additional carts - $30.00 per month.
            The charge for additional carts shall appear on the Customer’s
monthly Sewer/Water and Garbage bill.
         b.   Each customer shall be responsible for the reasonable care of its
refuse containers. Containers must be kept closed with lids or covers at all
times, as not to allow debris to escape or harbor mosquitoes, flies, rodents,
vermin or other disease carrying animals that create a nuisance, results in
noxious or offensive smells, or that is otherwise offensive or dangerous to the
public health.
      2.   Nonresidential Customers (Multi-Family and Commercial): Where fully
enclosed metal container systems exceeding thirty-two (32) gallons in capacity
are now in use at multi-family dwellings or commercial buildings, or where the
property owners request such systems or the waste hauler under contract with
the Town deems such system with respect to any multi-family dwellings or
commercial buildings where such containers are not in use, then fully enclosed
metal containers in excess of thirty-two (32) gallons in capacity shall be
provided by the waste hauler, or may be utilized by such customer if approved
by the waste hauler. With respect to such containers, the minimum bottom width
shall be no less than thirty-one (31) inches for one (1) cubic yard of
container space and the container shall be provided with outriggers.
         a.   Larger size containers shall be proportionately wider at the
bottom.
         b.   Containers having a capacity of four (4) cubic yards or more
shall be no higher than forty-three inches (43") with a four (4) piece lid
opening.
         c.   Containers shall meet federal and state safety standards.
      3.   Whenever containers in excess of thirty-two (32) gallon capacity are
used for multi-family or commercial buildings, the waste hauler under contract
with the Town shall furnish regularly scheduled collection service twice weekly
unless a compactor is provided by the property owner.
      4.   Containers, in excess of thirty-two (32) gallon capacity, used for
providing service to multi-family and commercial buildings shall be cleaned by
the waste hauler under contract with the Town at least quarterly or more often
if necessary, to keep them in sanitary condition. Any cleaning required more
frequently than once each quarter, as deemed necessary by the Town shall be at
the expense of the customer served.
      5.   Non-Customers: Each owner of a multi-family dwelling or a commercial
building in the District not serviced by the waste hauler under contract with
the Town, shall provide refuse containers specified in subsection B2 or a
waterproof dumpster with a close fitting lid for the collection and disposal of
refuse generated on the premises by the owner, tenants and occupants. All
refuse generated from such buildings shall be collected and disposed of in such
containers. Containers must be kept closed with lids or covers at all times as
to not allow debris to escape or harbor mosquitoes, flies, insects, rodents,
vermin or other disease carrying animals, that create a nuisance, results in
noxious or offensive smells, or that is otherwise offensive or dangerous to the
public health.
      6.   Disposal In Bags: All refuse to be disposed of pursuant to this
section shall first be placed in bags complying with subsection C below.
   C.   Refuse Bags: All refuse shall be disposed of in a closed or sealed bag,
except for large single items of refuse which do not fit in a standard garbage
bag but which fit in the containers described in subsection B of this section.
Refuse bags shall then be placed in containers described in said subsection B
of this section.
   D.   Availability Of Landfills Or Incinerators: All refuse haulers engaged
in waste collection and disposal in the district shall have available to them
at all relevant times one or more landfill sites or incinerators with all
necessary or appropriate federal, state, and local permits, licenses or
approvals for the operation of the disposal facility.
   E.   Waste Not Subject To Collection: Nonmunicipal waste, hazardous waste,
special waste, toxic waste, solid waste resulting from industrial or
manufacturing process, waste produced or generated as the result of
construction or repair activity (unless such construction or repair waste is
placed in a container that meets the requirements of subsections B and C of
this section), white goods, furniture and other similar items shall only be
disposed of by waste haulers and in disposal facilities having all necessary or
appropriate federal, state and local permits, licenses and approvals.
   F.   Cleanup Days: From time to time the town may designate a day or days
for the collection of large items from residential customers which are
otherwise not subject to collection. Subject to the town supervisor's
regulations and the requirement of subsection
3-4-4E of this chapter, miscellaneous waste items such as those described in
subsection E of this section may be placed out for collection on a public right
of way, adjacent to the owner's premises, on the cleanup day or days designated
by the town for collection and disposal.
   G.   Special Pick-Ups:
      1.   Customers/Covered Units:
         a.   Household Construction And Demolition Debris: The waste hauler
under contract with the Town, shall offer customers special pick-up services
for the collection of household construction and demolition debris in approved
containers when the quantity of such materials exceeds two (2) cubic yards, or
for large quantities of waste arising from residential move-ins or move-outs.
Special pick-up services shall be made available at least one time each week at
rates established in the contract between the Town and the waste hauler.
            (1)   The waste hauler shall provide the customer with an estimate
of the cost of a special pick-up service within forty eight (48) hours after
receiving a special pick-up request. The cost of such service shall be billed
to the customer by the waste hauler.
            (2)   Special pick-ups shall be accomplished within one (1) week
after requested by the customer.
         b.   Electronic Waste: The waste hauler under contract with the Town
shall provide for electronic waste and recycling if the customer calls ahead to
request the service. Electronic waste collection service shall be provided on
the same day as regular waste collection and at no additional cost to the
customer or Town. The waste hauler shall also provide gaylord boxes to the Town
for the purpose of collecting electronic waste at the Township Highway Garage.
The waste hauler shall remove and recycle all electronic waste collected
through the drop-off program at no additional cost to the Town.
         c.   Household Hazardous Waste: The waste hauler under contract with
the Town shall provide household hazardous waste collection and disposal if the
customer calls ahead to request the service. Household hazardous waste
collection shall be provided on the same day as regular waste collection at no
additional cost to the customer or Town.
         d.   White Goods/Bulk Items: Customers shall notify the waste hauler
under contract with the Town twenty-four (24) hours in advance for the
collection of White Goods or any bulk item weighing more than fifty (50)
pounds.
      2.   Non-Customers: Special pick-up collections of miscellaneous waste
items otherwise not subject to collection may be arranged by non-customers with
a licensed waste hauler. All special pick-ups will take place at such times
during normal business hours and days as may be mutually convenient for both
the non-customer and the waste hauler, subject to restrictions of subsection
3-3-4E of this chapter, provided such pick-up does not interfere with the
normal collection and disposal of waste under this chapter. (Ord. TO-92-1, 1-
14-1992; amd. Ord. TO-2014-5, 10-14-2014; Ord. 2019-6, 5-14-2019; Ord. TO-2021-
17, 12-14-2021; Ord. TO-2022-5, 4-12-2022)
3-4-9: WASTE HAULING LICENSE; PERMIT FEES:
   A.   License Required: It shall be unlawful to engage in waste removal,
collection and disposal in the District without first having secured a license
from the Town Clerk. All applications for waste hauling licenses shall be made
to the Town Clerk on forms provided by the Clerk.
   B.   Number Of Licenses: Only one license shall be issued and outstanding at
any given time to a waste hauler engaged in the removal of waste, collection
and disposal services within the District. A copy of the valid license must be
carried in all of the waste hauler's waste collection and transportation
vehicles serving properties within the District.
   C.   License Fee: The annual fee for a waste hauling license shall be as
follows:
      1.   No fee if the waste hauler is under contract with the Town to
provide waste removal, collection and disposal in the District.
      2.   Fifty dollars ($50.00) for each waste hauler engaged in the removal
of waste, collection and disposal for non-customers (multi-family buildings and
commercial property) within the District.
   D.   Term of License: Each waste hauling license issued hereunder shall be
valid for one (1) year, subject to the following conditions:
      1.   A license issued to a waste hauler pursuant to contractual
arrangements with the Town shall be valid only during the term of the contract
and in the absence of material default.
      2.   A license issued to a waste hauler without contractual arrangement
shall be null and void upon issuance of a license pursuant to contractual
arrangements with the Town for waste collection, removal and disposal services.
      3.   Failure to observe all requirements of this chapter shall be cause
for revocation of a waste hauling license.
   E.   Qualifications: An applicant for a waste hauling license shall
demonstrate the following qualifications:
      1.   The availability to the applicant of appropriate waste disposal
facilities duly permitted by the IEPA.
      2.   A sufficient number of modern, sanitary, leakproof waste collection
and transportation vehicles and equipment to provide efficient waste
collection, removal and disposal services.
      3.   Insurance meeting the requirements of subsection
3-4-4F10 of this chapter.
   F.   Permit Fees: Any property owner who rents a “roll-off” dumpster for the
owner’s property shall be required to apply for a Town permit the issued by the
Town Clerk. The permit fees are as follows:
      1.   Single family and two-family residential properties: Fifty dollars
($50.00) for each “roll-off” dumpster. The permit shall be valid for seven (7)
days.
      2.   Multi-family buildings and commercial properties: One hundred
dollars ($100.00) for each “roll-off” dumpster. The permit shall be valid for
thirty (30) days. (Ord. TO-92-1, 1-14-1992; amd. Ord. TO-2021-17, 12-14-2021;
Ord. TO-2022-13, 9-13-2022)
3-4-10: VIOLATIONS AS NUISANCES; ABATEMENT:
   A.   Declaration Of Nuisance: It shall be unlawful and it is hereby declared
to be a nuisance for any person to:
      1.   Deposit, abandon, dump, or place any waste, or cause any waste to be
deposited, abandoned, dumped or placed on any street, sidewalk, alley or other
public property; provided, this subsection shall not apply to any owner,
occupant or lessee of the premises who places waste generated on said premises
at the curbside of the abutting public street or other approved collection area
during the time provided in subsection
3-4-4E of this chapter prior to the time the waste is scheduled to be removed
by a licensed waste hauler, and provided that the waste is within containers
complying with this chapter;
      2.   Fail to provide for the removal and collection of waste as required
by this chapter and such failure results in a public nuisance;
      3.   Store, dump, or permit the accumulation of debris, refuse, garbage,
compost or any other waste in a matter that may harbor mosquitoes, flies,
insects, rodents, vermin or other disease carrying animals, that creates a
nuisance, results in noxious or offensive smells, or that is otherwise
offensive or dangerous to the public health;
      4.   Deposit, abandon, dump or dispose of any waste on any privately
owned property; provided that the owner, occupant or lessee of the property may
do so only as provided in subsections
3-4-4E and
3-4-6C of this chapter; and
      5.   Store, cast, throw, drop, place or deposit any waste in such a
manner that the waste may be carried by the action of the sun, wind, rain or
snow into or upon any street, sidewalk, alley, park or other public or private
place in the district or into or upon adjacent premises.
   B.   Authority To Abate: The town supervisor is hereby authorized to abate
any nuisance described in subsection A of this section.
   C.   Notice To Abate: The town clerk, at the direction of the town
supervisor, shall serve or cause to be served a notice to the owner, occupant
or lessee of any premises on which a nuisance exists, which notice shall demand
the abatement of the nuisance within seven (7) days. The owner may be served by
sending notice to the person who last paid the taxes on the real estate. (Ord.
SWO-2001-3, 9-18-2001)
   D.   Abatement By Township:
      1.   If the owner, occupant or lessee who is so notified does not abate
the nuisance within seven (7) days, as required by notice, the town supervisor
may provide for the abatement of the nuisance by township personnel or by
independent contractors.
